Current Commentary

The Riddle of the Current Situation 38

— Qing

Recently, the Japanese side has been vigorously attempting to disrupt North China. Various plans are being hatched, such as establishing a second puppet organization, coercing Puyi to enter the customs, or having the great powers jointly administer the region. Suddenly, rumors of Sino-Japanese compromise are spreading like wildfire. At the same time, Huang Fu, Chairman of the North China Political Affairs Committee, has absolutely denied the possibility of compromise, saying, "The situation in North China is so critical, how can there be compromise? Who would dare to talk about compromise?" His tone is firm, so we should believe that the talk of compromise is just a rumor.

However, observing the facts of recent days, we feel as if we are lost in a fog. Before the 17th, when our army was "withdrawing for strategic reasons to deploy new positions," the enemy army advanced fiercely like a storm. The situation in Peiping and Tianjin was extremely dangerous. The wind howled, the grass and trees seemed to be soldiers, and people were terrified. The whole country was shaken. However, after Huang Fu arrived in Peiping, the front line immediately entered a state of ceasefire. The enemy army stopped advancing, and the people of Peiping and Tianjin also felt "greatly relieved." According to reports, Huang Fu said that his trip was primarily to stabilize the morale of the people of North China. Now that he has succeeded, it seems that he has at least obtained the enemy's "understanding." Otherwise, how could Huang Fu's arrival in Peiping have suddenly caused the advancing enemy to halt? However, the rumors of compromise are indeed just rumors. This is why we find it puzzling.

Our country today lacks organization and strength. Some people believe that "resistance today is a meaningless sacrifice." We believe this is only a one-sided view. But what has led to this situation? It is the endless civil wars in recent years, political corruption, the inability to unite internally in the face of great disaster, and the indifference to the strong enemy. Those who compete for power and profit remain as before, and those who sing and dance merrily remain as before. What more can we say about this? However, our people are still seeking to strengthen themselves and are determined not to give up.

Moreover, recently, the authorities have often compared the gravity of the national crisis to a fire pit, saying that they themselves will jump into the fire pit. This statement seems right but is actually wrong. The so-called jumping into the fire pit is acceptable from an individual perspective. But today's problem is how to get our nation out of the fire pit. If everyone jumps into the fire pit, then there will only be mutual destruction. Those who jump into the fire pit will only drag others into the fire pit. Our people are already in deep water and burning fires. Today's demand is to get out of the water and fire and onto a comfortable mat, to figure out how everyone can jump out of the fire pit. If the authorities truly have a way to get everyone out of the fire pit in North China, then the people's hearts will naturally be stable. If the authorities temporarily jump into the fire pit, we will regard them as living Buddhas. Why worry about rumors?

Roosevelt's Peace Appeal

Our Country Accepts in Full 39

Reply Sent Yesterday, to be Announced Today

Two Points: Troops Not Crossing Borders, Military Preparations Not Expanding

Japanese Government Expresses Unwillingness to Agree Unconditionally

(Nanjing) The government's reply to President Roosevelt's appeal was meticulously drafted on the 19th. On the evening of the 19th, a telegram in the name of Chairman Lin was sent to President Roosevelt. The full text will be announced on the 20th. Before the official announcement of the reply, the authorities will not issue any opinions. (19th Central News Agency dispatch)

(Nanjing) Chairman Lin's reply to the US President is clear and simple. In addition to abstractly expressing full agreement with the four points of Roosevelt's proposal, he particularly praises the fourth step proposed by Roosevelt: that countries around the world should participate in a solemn and definite non-aggression pact, and each country should promise not to send armed forces of any nature beyond its borders. The actual problems of Japan's invasion of our Northeast four provinces and its attack on various parts of North China were not clearly mentioned. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The newspaper on the 19th reported that Foreign Minister Luo had made a statement on the matter. According to Foreign Minister Luo, at the request of a certain American newspaper, the Foreign Ministry issued a short statement in English on the 17th in the name of the Foreign Ministry spokesman, saying that President's declaration is a brave and powerful call for political and economic peace in the world. The reports in today's newspapers are either interpretations of that English statement by a certain agency, but it already has great differences from the original text. (19th Central News Agency dispatch)

Germany and Italy Willing to Cooperate

American Declaration Receives Strong Response 40

(London) German President Hindenburg sent a telegram to the US President, expressing his gratitude, saying that the plan proposed by the US President has received a strong response in Germany. The reply also quoted the words of the German Chancellor, saying that Germany is willing to cooperate selflessly with other countries to overcome current political and economic difficulties. (18th Reuters dispatch)

Rome The Italian Emperor sent a personal reply telegram to the US President, thanking him for issuing a noble message and expressing his fervent sympathy for the US President's proposal. At the same time, the Italian Ambassador to the United States, on behalf of the Italian government, sent a message to the US government, expressing its willingness to comply with the US President's initiative, praising the importance of the initiative, and saying, "The sincere cooperation of all those who desire world peace and happiness has never been as necessary as it is today, and the equal and appropriate importance of the rights of all countries without distinction has never been as urgent as it is today." The reply concludes by stating that the Italian government is prepared to join the United States and other governments in pursuing the realization of the US proposals in the most effective way possible. (18th Reuters dispatch)

Fourteen Countries Support American Proposal 41

Ankara Last night, the Turkish President telegraphed Roosevelt, expressing agreement with the various sections of Roosevelt's proposal. (19th Havas dispatch)

(Washington) Currently, the replying recipients already include England, France, Austria, Sweden, Denmark, Latvia, Norway, Netherlands, Cuba, Mexico, Panama, Switzerland, and Lithuania, a total of thirteen countries. However, it must be clarified that at this time, they are only accepting the principles stated by the US President, and not any specific document. (19th National News Agency dispatch)

Japan Decides to Attach Important Reservations 42

(Tokyo) Today, according to political circles here, Japan seems likely to endorse President Roosevelt's proposal in principle, but because of the abnormal state of affairs in neighboring countries, it will attach important reservations. Japan seems set to firmly declare that provocative weapons such as boycotts should be banned first, and then Japan can agree to unconditionally endorse the proposal. As for the issue of troops crossing borders, if the world is prepared to recognize the Great Wall as the border between China and "Manchukuo," then Japan can naturally agree. (19th Reuters dispatch)

(Tokyo) There are two points in President Roosevelt's peace appeal that the Japanese government finds difficult to accept: one is maintaining the status quo and not expanding military preparations, and the other is not crossing borders to advance troops. Because these two major principles are indeed contrary to Japan's continental policy, the Japanese government is unwilling to accept them unconditionally, but it cannot refuse, so it intends to accept them with conditions attached. It is reported that the conditions of reservation planned by the Japanese government are: (1) Recognizing "Manchukuo" as an independent country and drawing the Great Wall as the border between China and "Manchukuo"; (2) Permanently prohibiting China from boycotting Japanese goods. If these two conditions are accepted by the world, then Japan's national policy will not be hindered in any way. If "Manchukuo" is recognized as an independent country, Japan can expand its military preparations as much as possible in the name of "Manchukuo," and if China agrees to abolish the boycott of Japanese goods, Japan's demands will be fully achieved. Within these twenty years, Japan's internal situation will not have the extra strength to invade mainland China, so there is no need to cross borders to advance troops. It is heard that the Japanese Foreign Ministry is drafting a reply based on these two principles, submitting the original proposal to the Army and Navy Ministries for review, and then holding a joint meeting of the three ministries before sending a telegram reply to the US President. It is heard that the wording of the reply is very tactful, expressing its true intentions with the following words: (1) The purpose of the peace guarantee treaty promoted by the United States is only to promote the spirit of the Kellogg-Briand Pact. The Kellogg-Briand Pact recognizes the right of self-defense of all countries, and the new treaty should also recognize the right of self-defense of all countries. The Japanese government has never changed its position on this point. (2) Maintaining the status quo of military preparations is not a new proposal, and it is believed that it cannot prevent the expansion of military preparations permitted by the Washington Naval Treaty. (3) The principle of not crossing borders to advance troops should be limited to the nature of aggression. The dispatch of troops based on treaty obligations (such as the Japan-"Manchukuo" Protocol stipulating joint Japan-"Manchukuo" defense) and the advancement of troops to maintain order (such as invading Shanhaiguan) are naturally not subject to restrictions. Japan uses the above interpretations as principles that the new treaty should recognize, so there is no need to take a confrontational attitude. (19th China United Press dispatch)

Britain Seeks Opinions from Various Territories 43

(London) President Roosevelt's letter to 54 countries has been sent by the British government to the Prime Ministers of various autonomous territories for review. It is expected that after the British government seeks the opinions of the various territories, the British King will reply to President Roosevelt in the name of the entire British Empire. (18th Havas dispatch)

MacDonald Prepares to Draft Agreement 44

(Washington) It has recently been heard that British Prime Minister MacDonald may draft an agreement, including the US President's recommendations. It is said that Prime Minister MacDonald, after his frank talks at the White House, has fully understood the US President's intentions. The State Department is currently eagerly awaiting replies from Soviet Russia, Japan, and South American countries before considering the non-aggression and consultation conventions in Geneva. According to the replies from the thirteen European and American countries to date, none have mentioned any international disputes. The US President's original telegram also did not mention them, but the White House and the State Department are also well aware that such disputes are sufficient to hinder the replies of several countries. Therefore, it is expected that if an agreement is concluded in the future to accept not sending troops abroad, otherwise, the claim of recognizing the country as an aggressor must contain the words "henceforth," because officials all believe that troops already outside the country cannot be withdrawn immediately. As for today's Japanese Ambassador Debuchi's statement that Japan has no intention of advancing to the Peiping-Tianjin area, a good impression has been generated here. It is expected that there will be more clarifications of the situation in the near future. Therefore, US officials are currently awaiting further statements from the Japanese government. People in Washington are even more convinced that the situation in North China can be expected to not expand further because of the news that Chinese Finance Minister Song Ziwen will go to the White House again tomorrow afternoon to meet with the US President. (18th National News Agency dispatch)

Japanese Representative Ishii

Sends Courting Signals to the US 47

Japanese Ambassador to the US Broadcasts Atmosphere

Says Japan Has No Intention of Occupying Peiping and Tianjin

San Francisco Japanese representative Viscount Ishii gave a speech to the members of the Chamber of Commerce at the "Federal Club," saying that the recent talks by representatives of various countries in Washington were more than enough to clarify the international atmosphere and eliminate suspicion among countries. He also said that President Roosevelt has great foresight and is worthy of admiration. The points on which Japan and the United States cannot coordinate are few in number. In terms of commerce, Japan ranks third among American cargo customers, second only to the United Kingdom and Canada. Conversely, the United States is also one of Japan's most important customers. Therefore, in addition to some unimportant goods, the commerce between the two countries can supplement each other without competing with each other. On other issues, there are also very few cases where the major interests of the two countries conflict with each other. Japan is working hard to respect American interests in China, Manchuria, and Korea. Japan's overpopulation and the immigration problem are originally very serious, but Japan still respects the United States' views on Japanese immigration to the Americas. (18th Havas dispatch)

(Washington) Today, after Japanese Ambassador Debuchi visited US Undersecretary of State Phillips, he told reporters that Japan has no intention of entering the Peiping-Tianjin area. People here generally expect that Debuchi has already received new instructions from the Japanese government, so he visited the Undersecretary of State to clarify the situation in North China. According to Debuchi, he hopes to find a way to allow the Japanese army to withdraw immediately, but Debuchi did not say whether this method is already being negotiated, only falsely claiming that Japan recognizes the Great Wall as the boundary between China and "Manchukuo." Japan has long intended to withdraw its troops outside Shanhaiguan, but every time it attempts to withdraw its troops, it is repeatedly stopped due to pressure from the Chinese side. It is heard that Debuchi also discussed Japan's attitude towards the US President's non-aggression pact and general disarmament proposal during his meeting with Phillips. (18th National News Agency dispatch)

Brutally Killed by Japanese Army 48

Overseas Chinese in Manchuria, Under the Guise of Protection

Severely Monitored by Japan 49

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Home Affairs recently issued an order to protect and monitor foreign nationals residing in Japan. This monitoring will be further strengthened in the future, fearing that foreigners are acting as spies, especially fearing communist and anti-Japanese propaganda. This kind of monitoring may also contain the role of protecting foreign nationals, because since the activities of Japanese nationalists, incidents such as Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations and the abolition of the Japan-India Commercial Treaty, preparations are being made for an exclusion of foreigners, and the danger of an exclusion of foreigners can actually happen at any time. Therefore, the act of protecting foreign nationals is also necessary. (19th Havas dispatch)

Legislative Yuan Meeting 51

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its 18th meeting of the third session on the 19th. Sixty people attended, including Wang Qi, Ma Yinchu, and Fu Bingchang. Sun Ke chaired, and Liang Hancao was the secretary-general. The discussion items are as follows: (1) Review of the draft Food Management Law. Resolution: referred to the Legal System Committee together with the Economic Committee for review. (2) The Economic Committee of this Yuan, together with the Finance Committee and the Foreign Affairs Committee, reported on the review of the import goods, country of origin labeling regulations, and supplementary measures. Resolution: amended the first article of the import goods country of origin labeling regulations and passed it. (That is, a proviso is attached to the article, but in case of difficulties, the name of the country of origin may be marked in the language of the country of origin.) (3) Review of the Hunan National Salvation Public Bond case. Resolution: referred to the Finance Committee for review. When reviewing the second case, representatives from the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Ministry of Industry were all present to explain. The Finance Ministry representative explained that it is difficult to label foreign goods in Chinese characters during the production and transshipment of goods. The Foreign Ministry representative described the difficulties faced by the United Kingdom, the United States, France, and other countries after the Legislative Yuan passed the regulations when they made representations to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The Industry Ministry representative agreed to maintain the original proposal and did not need to amend it. After the attending Legislative Yuan members expressed their opinions in detail, the above resolution was made. (19th Central News Agency dispatch)

Case of Import Goods Marking Regulations 52

(Nanjing) The import goods country of origin marking regulations stipulate that when foreign goods are imported, they must be marked with Chinese characters on the packaging. Foreign businessmen all said that this would actually cause obstacles. Since the Central Political Conference referred the case to the Legislative Yuan for review, when the Legislative Yuan discussed the case on the 19th, the Ministry of Finance sent personnel to explain that the transshipment of various goods would be difficult after the regulations were implemented, so they must be amended. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent personnel to explain the situation after the United Kingdom, the United States, and France requested the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to amend the regulations. The Ministry of Industry sent personnel to advocate maintaining the original proposal. Then, Legislative Yuan members expressed their opinions in detail from the perspective of the country, which took a long time before making the decision of the assembly. (19th Central News Agency dispatch)

Page 8

Before the Opening of the World Economic Conference

First Seek to Stabilize Currency Values 61

Break Down Obstacles to the Discussion of Tariff Issues

England, America, France, and Germany Have Obtained Considerable Understanding

British King's Speech Will Be Broadcast Globally

(Washington) According to reliable sources, the rulers of the world's major financial countries are currently attempting to stabilize exchange rates, intending to complete the work before the opening of the World Economic Conference. This move is a direct result of the US President inviting politicians from various countries to meet. This movement is currently being led by US President Roosevelt, British Prime Minister MacDonald, French Prime Minister Daladier, Italian Finance Minister Junger, and German Deutsche Bank President Schacht. Although Japanese representative Ishii has not yet met with the US President, it is said that today, when Japanese Ambassador Debuchi visited Undersecretary of State Phillips, he indicated that Japan would join this group and advocate stabilizing the exchange market at prices close to the current exchange rate. It is expected that when the US President meets with Ishii in the future, this will be the first topic to be considered. According to what has been heard here, there has been considerable progress in terms of a general understanding among countries. When President and Prime Minister MacDonald first met, they decided that unless some understanding was reached before the World Economic Conference, the issue of exchange rates would be enough to hinder free and direct discussions on tariff issues. After several talks with MacDonald, they both felt that the exchange market and wheat prices were the two major obstacles to the conference, so they decided to attack these two issues first before the conference opened. Afterwards, politicians from other countries also agreed to this proposal. Therefore, the issue of wheat prices will also be raised at the Central European Grain Conference to be convened in Rome, Romania, on June 3. The conference will ask the representatives to discuss and adopt a method of managing production and prices, and the scope will be expanded. Representatives from all major wheat-producing countries will attend, and issues such as organizing or averaging grain tariffs and agreeing on export quotas that can be accepted by everyone will also be discussed.

▲ Washington Telegram from the National News Agency on the 19th. Today, the US President and Mexican Finance Minister Bini discussed stabilizing currency values for a long time, especially focusing on increasing the status of silver, because both countries are major silver producers. Afterwards, they issued a joint communique stating that the two countries will fully cooperate on economic and financial matters at the World Economic Conference. They also said that the two sides had a very successful discussion on the issue of stabilizing silver prices.

(London) When the British King gives his opening address at the World Economic Conference in London on June 12, he will issue the world's largest radio broadcast. The British King's speech will be transmitted from the Southern Gamsington Geological Museum to the Philadelphia International Telephone Bureau, and from there to the capitals of various European countries. As for the British Empire and the Americas, they can also hear the British King's speech from Rugby. It is estimated that all countries other than China and Japan can also hear this broadcast. (18th Reuters dispatch)

German Representative Announces Acceptance

MacDonald Disarmament Plan 62

American Representative Formally Proposes Non-Aggression Pact

Rumors of a Meeting Between French and German Prime Ministers in Geneva

(Geneva) At today's General Commission meeting of the Disarmament Conference, Chairman Henderson spoke, urging all representatives to compromise with each other and strive to conclude a convention. Henderson praised President Roosevelt's declaration, stating that it greatly contributed to the work of the Disarmament Conference. He then cited German Chancellor Hitler's speech on Wednesday, indicating that the German Chancellor now urged the Disarmament Conference to consider President Roosevelt's declaration with sympathy. After the Chairman's speech, German Representative Nadolny stated that Germany had decided to accept the disarmament plan proposed by British Prime Minister MacDonald. Nadolny, on behalf of the German government, declared acceptance of the British Prime Minister's plan, not only as a basis for discussion but also as the foundation for a future disarmament convention. He believed that this announcement was sufficient evidence of Germany's moderate spirit and willingness to cooperate, and hoped that other countries would also make every effort to adjust their interests within the scope of the British Prime Minister's plan. (Reuters, 19th)

(Washington) Today, the US State Department has instructed Davis, at the Geneva Disarmament Conference, to formally propose a non-aggression pact in accordance with the President's plan. It is reported that the US President's appeal to the heads of state of various countries for peace guarantees will be read at the General Commission of the Disarmament Conference, and Davis will also provide an explanation. Now that President Roosevelt's telegram has been issued, various countries have responded quickly, and the stalemate caused by Germany's demands is also expected to be resolved, which is very gratifying. (National News Agency, 18th)

(Paris) There are rumors that the French and German prime ministers will meet in Geneva next week. If true, the Disarmament Conference will definitely be revitalized. It is said that close friends of French Prime Minister Daladier are now urging the French Prime Minister to strive to meet with the German Prime Minister, as this is the best way to clarify the tense atmosphere. According to unofficial sources, plans for such a meeting are currently under study. It is now known that US Representative Davis first proposed the meeting between the two prime ministers to resolve the dilemma between France and Germany. The French side has not yet expressed its opinion, but it is generally believed that the French Prime Minister has accepted this suggestion. Since arriving in Europe, US Representative Davis has been engaged in extremely important behind-the-scenes work in international affairs. President Roosevelt's announcement to the world, issued before German Chancellor Hitler's address to Congress, was also at Davis's request. (Reuters, 18th)

(Geneva) The Disarmament Conference here is currently experiencing difficulties regarding the procedures to be adopted at the General Commission meeting of the Disarmament Conference on May 19th. The German side claims that German Chancellor Hitler has already explained Germany's position, so German Representative Nadolny does not need to make any further statements. Now, the French representative should disclose France's position, but the French side may not be ready to speak immediately, and French cabinet members will not be able to arrive in Geneva before May 19th. Therefore, it is generally expected that British Representative Eden will speak at that time, and Chairman Henderson may also express his views. (Reuters, 18th)

(Berlin) People here now believe that when the Geneva disarmament talks resume, France will not have explained Germany's demand for equality as German Chancellor Hitler explained it. What Hitler explained is that German armaments are completely equal to those of other countries in terms of quality and quantity. If France's explanation is not the same as Germany's, then the difficulties of the Geneva conference will be impossible to eliminate, because Germany has already declared its final word on this matter and cannot continue to make concessions. (Reuters, 18th)

(Washington) The White House and the State Department both exchanged messages with Davis, the disarmament representative in Europe, throughout the day. When the Disarmament Conference meets to discuss, Davis will issue a declaration in the name of the United States. The US government and Davis are exchanging messages to finalize the content of this declaration. Although the disarmament issue has major difficulties in terms of political technology, people in American political circles are still optimistic, believing that within ten days or so, before the London Economic Conference convenes, a convention can be concluded stipulating the first step in disarmament measures. The term will be set at five years, and it will stipulate that after the five-year term expires, Germany will enjoy equal rights to armaments in fact and in law. The general opinion is that the success of the convention depends on two facts: first, Germany sincerely promises to postpone the implementation of the principle of equality in armaments for five years; and second, France recognizes the abandonment of offensive weapons such as heavy artillery, bombing aircraft, tanks, and gas. The general opinion is that since Germany has no offensive weapons, it is materially impossible to cross the French border fortifications. It can be seen from this that the abolition of offensive weapons can obviously enhance France's security. (Havas, 18th)

(Geneva) The General Commission of the Disarmament Conference will meet at 3:30 pm. Chairman Henderson will first present recent events, then praise President Roosevelt's declaration, and mention Hitler's speech. Then, he will ask the Disarmament Conference to resume work and conclude as soon as possible. US Representative Davis will respond on behalf of President Roosevelt. German Representative Nadolny arrived here by plane at 10:00 this morning, seemingly wanting to reiterate certain parts of Hitler's speech in a "Geneva-style tone." Nadolny will also invite delegations from various countries to explain their opinions separately. British Representative Eden met with Henderson this morning, and he may deliver a speech. It is generally speculated that Germany will use a means, supported by Italy, to force Britain and France to reciprocate with corresponding sacrifices for "Germany's concessions." (Havas, 19th)

(London) After exchanging messages with Foreign Minister Simon and Disarmament Conference Representative Eden, it has been decided that he will go to Geneva on Monday to attend the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting and participate in the work after the reopening of the Disarmament Conference. (Havas, 19th)

Free Transportation for Japanese Troops 64

(Tokyo) The content of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' rebuttal to Soviet Deputy Foreign Minister Karakhan's protest regarding the Middle East Road dispute is as follows: (1) The Japanese government's policy of justly recognizing the Soviet government's interests in the Middle East Road and respecting Soviet interests after "Manchukuo" remains unchanged. (2) However, the Japanese government is not responsible for the actions of Japanese officials in "Manchukuo." (3) The cause of the Middle East Road dispute is that the Soviet Union has illegally oppressed "Manchukuo" in the exercise of its legitimate rights, so the Soviet Union should reflect on itself. (4) The Soviet Union's protest against Japan regarding the issue of unpaid transportation fees is unreasonable. The purpose of the Japanese army's actions is to protect the Middle East Road, so it should naturally transport Japanese troops free of charge. The transportation fees currently unpaid by the Japanese army are for the transportation of vehicles, horses, and food. After the discount rate is determined, the full amount will naturally be paid. Anglo-Japanese Trade Issues 65

Matsudaira Negotiates with Britain:

Agreement in Principle Reached

Notice of Abolition of the West-Fife Commercial Treaty

Japanese Cotton Industry's Hatred of Britain Deepens

(Tokyo) Matsudaira, the Japanese ambassador to Britain, reported to the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday that, regarding the Indo-Japanese Commercial Treaty issue, Matsudaira and the British Trade Minister, the Matsuyama Business Officer stationed in Britain, and the British Business Officer negotiated separately. As a result, the two sides agreed in principle: (1) In order to revise the overall Anglo-Japanese commercial agreement, a council of commercial and industrial representatives from both countries should be convened to discuss the compromise conditions that both sides should take in trade, and a new commercial treaty should be formulated based on the results of the discussion. (2) The agreement should first determine the number of imports and exports of major trade goods and divide the markets for the goods of the two countries to avoid conflicts between the two countries. Negotiations will proceed according to this principle. It is reported that the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs received this news and discussed countermeasures with the Ministry of Commerce and Industry this morning. It will send a telegram to Ambassador Matsudaira within days to put forward specific conditions and then proceed with the second step of negotiations. (China United Press, 19th)

Britain has no "sincerity," and Japan should not continue to take a wait-and-see attitude and sit idly by. It must change its attitude from now on and resolve to fight Britain. Page 9

French Parliament Approves

Non-Aggression Treaty with Russia 98

Pengu Claims Efforts to Secure Agreement with Italy

▲Reuters, Paris, 18th - The French Chamber of Deputies unanimously passed a motion tonight, supporting the exchange of ratification documents for the Franco-Russian Non-Aggression Pact signed in Paris on November 29th of last year. Former Prime Minister Herriot and Foreign Minister Pengu both attended and delivered speeches. 520 members of parliament were present.

▲Havas, Paris, 18th - The Chamber of Deputies voted to ratify the Franco-Russian Non-Aggression Treaty resolution. 520 members voted, and all were in favor. The Socialist Party spokesman recognized the treaty as a tool for building peace and therefore also supported the motion. Former Prime Minister Herriot then provided some explanations regarding the Franco-Russian treaty, as he was the one who prepared it and signed it. Herriot said, "This treaty can maintain maximum security and effectively eliminate all economic and political aggression." The Little Entente countries and Romania have all recognized this treaty, so it is clear that its purpose is not to oppose any country. Finally, Herriot explained the immediate effects that the treaty can achieve, namely: (1) Soviet Russia has come forward in Geneva to advocate for the definition of "aggressor nations," and (2) Soviet Russia is therefore opposed to revising treaties. Foreign Minister Pengu followed with a speech, stating that we have great confidence in this treaty and have no reason to doubt the sincerity of the other signatory nation. The government attaches great importance to this treaty, which is evident in the changed attitude of the Soviet representative at the Disarmament Conference. Furthermore, France's traditional policy is to continue expanding the scope of its alliances without abandoning previous alliances. The Non-Aggression Treaty concluded between France and Soviet Russia is fully in line with France's traditional policy. Therefore, the French government is now striving to coordinate with Italy. The Foreign Minister further briefly explained the significance of the Non-Aggression Treaty, stating, "We will not adopt any aggressive attitude towards Soviet Russia, nor will we even take economic measures to jointly exclude Soviet Russia. We will absolutely not interfere in Soviet Russia's internal affairs. We also believe, based on the principle of reciprocity, that the other party will also respect its promises and cease all propaganda against our country's policies. Furthermore, our attitude towards any country's exiles will not be changed because of this." In conclusion, the Chamber of Deputies passed the ratification motion, stating that "the Franco-Russian Non-Aggression Treaty can consolidate peace and promote the common interests of European countries. This Chamber of Deputies accepts the exchange of ratification documents with satisfaction."

Division of New Defense Lines After Our Army's Retreat 99

— Rate

Forming an Arc-Shaped Position from Gubeikou to Lutai

Weng's Troops Defend Fengrun, Japanese Planes Bombard Heavily

A special dispatch from Peiping reports that our frontline troops have been retreating step by step in recent days, and the Japanese army is advancing steadily. The situation in Peiping and Tianjin is extremely tense, with rumors rampant and everyone on edge. However, the fighting has not been intense. West of Luanzhou is mostly flat terrain, and it is almost impossible to defend against the Japanese artillery fire. After our troops in Tangshan retreated westward, a unit of Japanese cavalry was discovered in the Majiakou area. The situation in Tangshan is unclear, and public order is extremely chaotic. Unscrupulous individuals are taking the opportunity to rob, rape, murder, and commit all kinds of atrocities. Wan Fulin's troops suffered heavy losses due to disrupted communication during the fighting, resulting in each unit fighting on its own. Wan himself has already taken a special train west. His troops are extremely exhausted, and it has been decided to withdraw them to the rear for rest and reorganization in Yangcun, awaiting orders to fight the enemy. He Zhuguo is currently in Lutai, with a portion of his troops remaining on guard near Xugezhuang. Our defense line has been reorganized, forming an arc-shaped position from the Gubeikou line to Lutai on the front of the Beining Railway, including Miyun, Pinggu, Jixian, Ninghe, and Lutai, as the foremost line of defense. Since the abandonment of Luanzhou, our army's formation has been renewed. Currently, He Zhuguo's troops are defending the front of the Beining Road, and Wang Yizhe's troops are near Yutian, with considerable strength remaining. As for the Xifengkou line, Song Zheyuan's troops have undergone some changes in their lines due to pressure from the rear, with most of them retreating from Longjingguan and Santunying via Zunhua. Song Zheyuan himself is deploying military forces in Jixian, building new positions between Zunhua and Jixian to continue resisting the Japanese army. The closest line in front of Miyun is still in the Jiusongling area, and there has been no fighting today or yesterday.

Weng Zhaoyuan personally led his troops to defend Fengrun for three days and three nights, eventually withdrawing due to being outnumbered and outgunned. After Weng's troops withdrew, the Japanese army did not dare to advance rashly, sending out advance scouts to reconnoiter. After learning that our troops had retreated, they then drove their army into the city and followed to the east of Yutian, where a small engagement occurred at Liangjiadian. Wang Yizhe's troops are continuing to retreat to the west of Yutian. This reporter went to a Peiping office this morning (the 17th) to gather news and encountered a soldier from Weng's troops who had been slightly wounded on the front line. Disguised as a fried dough stick vendor, he secretly returned to Peiping from Fengrun. According to him, Weng's troops defended Fengrun for three days and nights, with only eighty soldiers in the entire garrison. The Japanese army used fierce artillery fire, attacking the city in shifts. These few defending soldiers were killed and wounded one after another, almost all sacrificing themselves. Only three to five survivors remained. After the Japanese army entered the city, they encountered our wounded soldiers. After inquiring about the situation of the defense, they also sighed and expressed sympathy. They shook their heads in disbelief at the fact that a very small number of people had defended a city for three days. Weng himself escaped alone in a car when withdrawing from Fengrun. He was chased by Japanese planes several times along the way. The road was rugged, and the car traveled slowly on the bumpy dirt road. Weng often got out of the car to push and pull it forward. Later, Weng, fearing danger due to the frequent bombing by Japanese planes, sought another path to escape, thus avoiding disaster. His car driver drove the car back to Peiping this morning. According to him, the Japanese planes bombed the villages near Fengrun indiscriminately, committing inhumane acts. In one place, an old man, seeing a Japanese plane coming, staggered toward a cellar outside the village with his granddaughter. But a Japanese bomb had already arrived. With a loud explosion, they fell to the ground. Grandfather and granddaughter died side by side next to the cellar. A leg flew to the top of a tree, blood dripping and staining the ground red. The corpses were divided into several sections, scattered on the ground. Their clothes were burned by the bomb fire, and a stench filled the air. Passersby covered their noses and passed by. Afterwards, the residents fled, leaving the area deserted, which is also very pitiful. (17th)

Feng Zhanhai's Army Sheds Blood at "Da Liang Di" 100

Special Correspondent Guo An

(1)

A special dispatch from Zhangjiakou reports that since the Volunteer Army rose up in various parts of eastern Jilin after the September 18th Incident, General Feng Zhanhai, with the strength of a single regiment, called on patriotic volunteers and contacted the Guo, Yao, and other Volunteer Armies, fighting in the vast plains of the Black Water and White Mountains. By the autumn of last year, due to a lack of ammunition and rear support, and under the combined pressure of enemy aircraft and heavy artillery fire, after sacrificing a number of patriots, they finally reached the territory of Rehe Province. Before the rear could replenish ammunition and supplies, the enemy began to attack Rehe. General Feng defended the lines of Kailu and Chifeng, resisting for a week. However, the treacherous actions of Cui and Liu, who had lost their minds and sided with the enemy, affected the overall progress and retreat of the battle. He had no choice but to retreat to Dolon via side roads. The weather was bitterly cold, and the north wind blew snow. The brothers, in single clothing and with iron spears, climbed mountains and crossed ridges, concentrating in Dolon. At that time, the call for the enemy to attack Chahar rose again. Feng's army made some adjustments and prepared to resist. Later, due to extreme material difficulties, Feng's army received orders to temporarily retreat to the rear for reorganization. From then on, the defense of Dolon was taken over by Zhao's Cavalry Army. The outskirts of Guyuan to Dolon were still under defense. Soon, the army was ordered to be reorganized into the □□□ Division. All the original horses were handed over to Peiping, transforming them into infantry. The horses of the army all belonged to farmers in the northeastern countryside. The brothers in the Volunteer Army all came from the countryside, bringing their own guns and horses, and had been fighting bloody battles against the Japanese. Each person's horse was a companion who had worked hard together through life and death. Once they left their horses, many of the brothers shed tears, as if they were parting with family. After General Feng Zhanhai's army was reorganized into the infantry □□□ Army, the places they garrisoned were all in the countryside. However, these anti-Japanese heroes who came from the countryside had very harmonious feelings with the local people. For example, the town of Pingdingpu within the territory of Zhangyuan County has always been protected by the church. No troops could pass through, let alone stay there. However, since Feng's army garrisoned there, the soldiers were disciplined, and the town requested General Feng to station some troops in the town to protect the merchants and residents. General Feng had no choice but to set up a staff office in Pingdingpu Town, in order to facilitate military communication with Guyuan. Therefore, General Feng Zhanhai's subordinates also got along well with the people. After the fall of Dolon, Zhao Chengzhou's five cavalry regiments retreated to Zhangbei County and concentrated there. In this way, the first-line troops were all the □□□ Army. General Feng Zhanhai moved into Pingdingpu to command nearby. On the 4th and 5th, enemy and puppet troops, including Liu Guitang, numbering over 2,000, attempted to attack "Da Liang Di," but were repeatedly repelled by Feng's army. Apart from artillery test shots every day, there was no sign of them moving south. At this time, General Feng believed that there was an opportunity to counterattack, to recover Dolon and consolidate the defense of eastern Chahar. Therefore, he made careful plans. The attacking force consisted of a brigade and two regiments, the brigade commander's surname was Zhao, and the other two regiments were one cavalry and one infantry, with the cavalry regiment commander surnamed Sun, and the infantry regiment commander surnamed Wang. On the night of the 8th, this attacking force, under the command of General Feng, entered the attack preparation position. In addition to a battalion of attached artillery, including mountain, field, and mortar guns, there were also fifteen heavy machine guns, and a large number of light machine guns and automatic rifles. Each soldier was attached with six hand grenades. That night, preparations were completed, and they began to advance and attack at dawn on the 9th. Thus, the bloody battle of "Da Liang Di" began.

(2)

The sound of artillery had already moved and fluctuated with the gray-yellow light of the sky on that vast sandy plain. Army Commander Feng stood resolutely by the earth fortress of the artillery observation post. At this time, the enemy and puppet army was unexpectedly thrown into chaos by the concentrated artillery fire of Feng's army. During that chaotic moment, the enemy and puppet army's mountain and field guns also entered the position, shaking the ground with their bombardment. But under these circumstances, the artillery fire of Feng's army had undoubtedly completed the purpose of suppression fire. Although the enemy frantically fired a barrage of chaotic shots, at this time, the sound of Feng's army's attack advance号suddenly sounded in the yellow sand that covered the sun. Brigade Commander Zhao, holding a broadsword in his hand, urged his brothers forward. The sound of machine guns and rifles was gurgling like boiling water. The enemy and puppet army, watching Feng's army like a tide, although they still dared to ambush in those insecure trenches, after firing a volley of guns into the air, they all rushed to the horse posts, grabbed their horses, and fled towards Dolon. The entire line of the rebel army was shaking. Army Commander Feng saw it very clearly through binoculars. At this time, it was 11 o'clock in the morning. Sun Heqi's cavalry regiment had long been on horseback there, preparing to attack. The order to pursue had just been spoken by Army Commander Feng, but who knew that the broken line of the enemy and puppet army suddenly stopped. It turned out that the Japanese army's reinforcements, sitting in trucks, had rushed from Dolon to reinforce them. So those rebel troops, under the pressure of the Japanese army, had no choice but to turn around and counterattack. At this time, Feng's army's line had already become the pace of attack. Army Commander Feng frowned when he saw this critical situation, and called out for the bugler to continue blowing the charge号. So, the hearts of every younger brother were filled with a chamber of revenge, ready to sprinkle it on this vast battlefield丨Da Liang Di丨. (To be continued)

Guangdong Province Establishes

Political Research Association 101

Researching the Implementation of a Three-Year Governance Plan

With Heads of Military and Civilian Agencies as Members

Guangzhou Correspondence: Guangdong Province previously formulated a three-year governance plan to be implemented on schedule. However, the beginning of reforms cannot be achieved overnight, and even more so, the implementation requires the cooperation of various military and civilian agencies. Therefore, the First Army Group Headquarters and the Guangdong Provincial Government recently initiated the formation of a Guangdong Provincial Political Research Association in order to study the implementation of the plan. It was established yesterday at the Provincial Government. The main organizational points of the Political Research Association are as follows: Members include the Commander-in-Chief of the First Army Group, the Chairman of the Guangdong Provincial Government, members of the Provincial Party Headquarters and City Party Headquarters, generals of the land and air forces stationed in the province, secretaries and directors, the director of the Political Training Office of the First Army Group, the director of the Political Training Office of the military headquarters, the secretary-general of the Provincial Government Committee, directors and chief secretaries of various departments, the mayor of Guangzhou and the directors of subordinate bureaus, the president of the High Court, the president of the District Court, the Salt Transport Envoy, the Superintendent of the Yuehai Customs, the inspector of foreign affairs of the five provinces, the president and vice president of the Provincial Bank, the director of the Railway Bureau, the director of the Public Security Bureau, the director of the Investigation and Statistics Bureau, the director of the Agriculture and Forestry Bureau, the director of the Port Authority, the director of the Telecommunications Administration, the director of the Highway Administration, the magistrates of Nanhai and Panyu counties, special appointees of the headquarters and the provincial government. In addition, land, sea, and air force generals stationed outside the province and county magistrates outside the city who come to the province on business should also join as temporary members. The association has a secretariat, organized by personnel dispatched from the headquarters and the provincial government, to manage all documents and general affairs. Meetings are held on the second Saturday and Sunday of each month, and the fourth Saturday and Sunday, from 4:00 PM to 6:00 PM. If members have opinions on various issues, they should submit them to the association's secretariat three days before the meeting, except in special circumstances, so that they can be submitted for research. In addition to the secretariat, the association has political, educational, social, transportation, legal, military, and diplomatic groups. Each group has a leader, appointed by the chairman from among the members. All kinds of problems should be submitted to the respective groups for study before being presented separately for discussion. If problems are considered to require further review after discussion, the chairman will temporarily designate members to review them. Members must strictly maintain the confidentiality of the research content until the time of publication. (May 12)

Xuzhou Suffers Torrential Rain Disaster 102

River Waters Overflow, Wheat Seedlings Damaged

County Farmers' Association Submits Petition to County for Relief

Xuzhou Correspondence: In recent years, the river channels have been blocked and have long lacked dredging. The residents in the urban area mostly freely fill the river, resulting in a loss of both storage and discharge capacity. Whenever there is heavy rainfall, they suffer from flooding. The torrential rains last summer turned the entire area into a swamp. For the past two years, the authorities have remained indifferent to water conservancy. The rainfall this spring has been more than in previous years. Since the 13th of this month, the heavy rain has not stopped, and today (the 18th) it has still not cleared up. The flood disaster is reported again. According to the investigation, in the first district, the Wenqugou in the city is blocked and impassable. Areas along the river such as the Confucius Temple and Doumu Palace are flooded to the ankles, and transportation is blocked. The Kui River outside the city is overflowing, and the water has flowed back. The amount of water in the former course of the Yellow River has increased sharply. In the second, third, and fifth districts, which are near Weishan Lake, most of the wheat seedlings have been flooded. The water is deeper in the seventh district. Farmlands in the areas of Sanbu Township, Guanqiao Town, Wucun Township, Yuzhuang Township, Zhongshan Township, and Qinzhai Township are flooded, with the water reaching four or five feet deep in low-lying areas. In the eighth district, low-lying fields in Shuanggu Town, Jiuji, Jiazhai, and Dawangji have also been flooded. The twelfth district belongs to the Gaogong River basin. Along the Longhai Railway near Daxujia, the water is one foot deep on the flat ground north of the road. The rainfall this time is very widespread, so the districts have reported disasters one after another. Yesterday, more than a dozen representatives of the disaster-stricken people, including Teng Shaosheng and Liu Guangrun, came to the city to petition the county government, urging them to quickly find a way to provide relief and stating that if the river channels could be dredged, the villagers would be willing to automatically provide labor. The County Farmers' Association also reported the disaster to the county based on the villagers' reports, specifically submitting a document stating, "Submitting a report to relay the disaster situation, earnestly requesting the dispatch of personnel to investigate and coordinate relief to stabilize people's livelihoods. According to Liu Guangrun, the director of the Yumin District Farmers' Association, on the 13th of this month, there was thunder and rain, which did not stop all day. It was even worse in the evening, with torrential rain pouring down. By dawn on the 14th, the water depth in the villages of Sibudun, Sibu Lake, Shanglou, Yanying, Dongshantou, Sanbu, Haihu, Xialou, and Tengzhuang in the southwest of the seventh district was 4 to 6 feet deep on the flat ground, and the wheat seedlings were completely lost to the water. The number of other affected areas is unknown. At this time when the new crop is not yet available, the disaster is sudden, and the farmers are panicked and helpless, appearing to have no way to seek death. Wheat is the people's lifeblood. Once it is flooded, I am afraid that the heavens will stir up thoughts of change, and there will be unrest in social order. I earnestly request that it be quickly forwarded to the county government, sending personnel to investigate and verify, and seek relief, and dredge the river channels to avoid further disasters. Furthermore, according to verbal reports from farmers in other districts who have come to the association one after another, the rainfall this time is extremely heavy, and low-lying fields are all flooded, with the disaster situation being extremely serious. Considering that the national crisis is imminent and banditry is spreading, the rural economy has already fallen into bankruptcy. How can the heavens not have pity and suddenly bring down this calamity? In addition to urging each district by telephone to rush to report the disaster situation in detail, it is appropriate to first prepare a document to forward it for your assessment and approval, and quickly dispatch personnel to investigate and verify and coordinate relief, awaiting orders to the utmost." County Magistrate She Nianci, considering that the disaster situation in the seventh district was particularly serious, took the Jinpu train to Sanbu today (the 18th), got off, and went to conduct an on-site investigation to devise a relief plan. However, the intermittent rain is still a cause for concern. According to the investigation, the main rivers in Xuzhou include the Kui River in the south of the city, which relies on it to discharge the water from the city, the Wangzhou River, which relies on it to discharge the water from the mountains south of the city, and the water from Sibu and Sanbu Lakes also rely on it for discharge. In the north of the city, there is the Jingshan River, which receives water from Weishan Lake and flows down into Pizhou. The Fangting River is used to discharge water from the mountains north of the city. The branches of these main lines have lacked dredging for years. If they are not thoroughly dredged, the flood disaster cannot be eliminated. (18th)

Indictment Filed in the Jiang Pingfan Assassination Case 103

Court Prosecutor Indicts for Premeditated Murder

More Than Ten Townships Organize Huang Sandi Support Association

Fuzhou Correspondence: The case of the assassination of Jiang Pingfan, the Superintendent of the Minhai Customs, has been transferred to the Minhou District Court Prosecutor's Office and handled by Prosecutor Xu Guanlan. The investigation has now been completed, and an indictment was filed on the 13th, stating that the murderer Huang Sandi was only back in Fujian from Taiwan for nine days, yet he was able to recognize the victim's chartered car and carried a sharp knife and ash bag, waiting at the scene of the crime for several days. Before the murder, after returning to Fujian, he took a photo in the Guanghua Photo Studio in the costume of a magistrate executing a judge. (According to the plot of this play, a retired judge covets someone's cemetery, forces them to give it up, and then kills them and occupies the land. Later, a new magistrate arrives, learns the truth, and sentences the judge to death as compensation.) Based on the above points, it is concluded that his murderous act was based on the result of deep thought and consideration, and had a definite plan before and after its implementation. He committed the crime of premeditated murder under Article 284 of the Criminal Code and should be sentenced to death. However, the defendant is a worker with a simple mind, harboring grievances over his father's grave, leading to resentment, which turned into hatred. While his crime deserves punishment, his situation is not without pity. It seems that he should be sentenced in accordance with Article 77 of the same law, which states that if the circumstances of the crime are pitiful, the penalty may be reduced. Currently, the Fuzhou community is paying close attention to this case. Jiang's friends, including Lin Zhiyuan, a member of the Provincial Government Committee, Wang Huaijin, a member of the Provincial Party Headquarters, Lin Yushi, a secretary of the National Government, Shi Jialin, the former Director of the Department of Finance, Huang Zhanyun, the former Director of the Department of Agriculture and Industry, Chen Wei, the captain of the Security Team, and dozens of other important figures in the party, government, and military circles, have initiated the organization of the Jiang Daoyi Comrades Funeral Office to handle the litigation, aiming to achieve the goal of punishing the murderer and avenging the crime. The people of more than ten townships, including Houpu, Qianyu, Xucuo, and Fengban in Dongmen, have also initiated the organization of the Huang Sandi Support Association, submitting public appeals for Huang's defense and raising funds for Huang's legal expenses. The Lawyers Association has also appointed Chen Hengquan, Huang Shang, and Lin Dan to serve as Huang's voluntary defense counsel. The two sides are evenly matched, and the outcome is difficult to predict. (15th)

Wuxi

Vigorously Expanding Defense Efforts 106

Wuxi County Magistrate Yan Shenyu believes that the county's defense regiment is related to local security and is determined to thoroughly rectify it, and will not be frustrated by the current achievements. Currently, there are 60 training centers that have been established in the city and countryside, with a total of 2,520 militiamen. In the future, it will be actively expanded to 85 Jia. In addition to reorganizing the merchant regiments, local strong young men will be recruited to serve as militiamen in order to train a strong army to defend the locality. As for the funding issue, in addition to the inherent 21,000 yuan, it has been decided that the store donation will be levied at 10% along with the house donation, amounting to about 50 yuan per year. As for the donations from gentry and wealthy people and special products, it has been decided to postpone the collection for the time being. In addition, the automobile and shipping donations were also decided to be levied first yesterday, and the principles are: (1) 5 Li will be levied per ticket with the ticket price; (2) The two donations are assumed to be 5,000 yuan; (3) Included in the general budget, allocated as the Jia brand business expenses.

Illegal Drugs Discovered at Ruizheng Cocoon Warehouse 107

According to a tip, the Jiangyin Fourth Branch of the Narcotics Investigation Office suspected that the Ruizheng Cocoon Warehouse under the Wuxi Gongyun Bridge was manufacturing drug pills. Therefore, investigator Yao Lemin and informant Ding and others were dispatched by car to Wuxi and went directly to the warehouse to search. Three burlap bags of raw materials for manufacturing drug pills were found upstairs, and Zhang Yanbin, an employee of the warehouse, was taken into custody for interrogation.

Wujiang

Strong Winds Collapse Houses, Injuring People 108

At 7:40 PM on the 16th, dark clouds suddenly gathered in Zhezhen Town, and wind and rain swept in, blowing down the houses of seven families, including the Shengpinglou Sauce Garden in Dongzha, injuring more than 70 people and killing five people, including an old woman from the bamboo ware store and an 18-year-old girl from the pastry shop. After the incident, local agencies specially organized a temporary hospital in the Chenghuang Temple to rescue the injured. The disaster caused great losses and was truly a catastrophe for Zhezhen. The other towns of Pingwang and Beizhu were also hit by windstorms. Fortunately, the houses collapsed but no one was injured. In Langdachuan in this city, all the thatched houses of the out-of-town residents were blown down. The long-distance telephone lines from Wujiang to Zhezhen were completely broken, and many of the Suzhou telegraph poles were also blown down. The losses from this incident are shocking.

Changzhou

A Traitor Arrested at a Train Station 109

A railway police officer from the 5th section of the Wuyi Railway Station Police Division arrested a traitor on the evening of the 17th. Upon interrogation, the traitor identified himself as Wang Jinkui. He was carrying a small flag, a mirror, and had a shaved head except for a tuft of long hair on top, about the size of a silver dollar, shaped like a peach. He wore a peaked cap, a gray old coat, and torn shoes. The railway police took him to the division, where he was taken away by the station's military police. The suspect readily admitted to infiltrating the interior as an enemy to gather intelligence. On the 18th, Magistrate Cai brought the suspect to the office for interrogation. The suspect confessed to his past intelligence-gathering activities, including secret codes used by his accomplices, and mentioned visiting Kunshan, Suzhou, Wuxi, and even Changzhou. After the interrogation, he was sent back to the military police camp and will be sent to the Capital Garrison Headquarters for further investigation soon.

The county government received a report from the Daqiao Chamber of Commerce stating that a firewood merchant, Xu Qizhi, hired a sailboat to go to Jiangnan to purchase river firewood. While passing the Sifang Bridge area across from Renfu Township in Xinzhou, they were suddenly attacked by a dozen bandits, all speaking with a Pizhou accent. Dong Xisheng, a soldier from the 3rd squad of the Linze Town Police Division in the 10th District garrison, committed suicide by hanging himself the other night in the squad headquarters while others were asleep due to the county government's large arrears in salary and the lack of funds to treat his toxic sores, which led him to become disillusioned with life. By the time he was discovered, he had already died. This is indeed tragic.

Xiaoshan

Mother and Son Commit Suicide Due to Poverty and Suffering 112

In Zhengjia Li outside the South Gate of Xiaoshan, a civilian named Zheng Wenzhi, 24 years old, worked in a Beijing goods store in Shanghai. He lost his job and returned to his hometown last month and contracted typhoid fever, preventing him from getting out of bed. As a result, his family of four had no means of survival. On the night of the 17th, he secretly drank a bowl of bittern salt in the kitchen and died. His 70-year-old mother, seeing that her son was poor and ill and unable to make a living, committed suicide by throwing herself into the Nanmen River on the morning of the 18th. By the time neighbors realized what had happened, she had already died.

Bengbu

The Truth Behind the Traitorous Conspiracy 113

The military and police supervisory office here recently cracked down on a large number of traitors in Bengbu. After interrogation, they have been sent to Xuzhou to be dealt with by the Jinpu Garrison Headquarters. According to insiders familiar with the truth from the cracked reactionary organizations, the key arrestees are Ma Yansheng, the head and commander-in-chief of the People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army, Zhang Zhongjing, the deputy head, and 14 others suspected of assisting the enemy, including Zhang Xiaolian and Shi Yuewu. Ma and Zhang confessed that they were instructed by a general in Peiping and a chairman of a Buddhist association, but did not mention receiving any official commission. However, based on the facts of secret agent reports and the evidence and testimony, it is believed that the traitors Ma Yansheng and Zhang Zhongjing were indeed swayed by profit and engaged in activities that harmed the country, making them traitors. Their reactionary points are sevenfold: (1) They established titles and summoned bandits without being commissioned by anyone or registering with the government. (2) They created flags and seals without authorization, and the flag style was vastly different from the Party and national flag style. (3) They used cunning names to bewitch the ignorant people. (4) They were instructed by a Siamese named Li Congzhi. (5) They received huge amounts of money from the puppet state. (6) They seemed to follow the orders of the Post-Heavenly Salvation Sect leader and the troops imitated the Qing Dynasty's organization, which involved suspicion of preserving the monarchy. (7) They planned a riot to burn and loot Bengbu, echoing the Japanese invaders. Fortunately, the crackdown occurred early, so the traitors' plans failed.

Page 10

Local News

Amidst the Ceasefire Rumors in North China

News Received from Various Sources in This City 114

Both China and Japan Believe a Ceasefire is Possible

Wang Zhengting Believes the Sino-Japanese Issue is International

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, after the newly appointed Chairman of the North China Political Affairs Committee, Huang Fu, arrived in Peiping, it was widely rumored in this city that China and Japan were moving towards a compromise. Although Huang has repeatedly stated that he will never sign any agreement, and the Japanese consulate in this city has also denied the rumored two compromise conditions, external speculation is still rife. With Rehe lost, whether the Japanese army will attack Peiping and Tianjin is of great concern to the entire nation. Yesterday, a reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency learned that China and Japan had once discussed this matter in Shanghai, but it is difficult to predict whether it will be realized in the future. Judging from the remarks of former Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, he also said that there is a possibility of a ceasefire, but the reality is still far away. When there is a possibility of negotiation in the future, the Japanese side indicated that it will send representatives from the military, and Minister Yoshizawa will not go north for the time being. The details are recorded as follows:

Meeting with Yoshizawa Akira 115

Yesterday, it was rumored that the compromise on the Sino-Japanese military affairs in the north was discussed several times by Huang Fu and Japanese Minister Yoshizawa Akira, because there were rumors of two conditions: "The two sides understand that the Chinese army will temporarily station south of the Luan River, then the Japanese army will withdraw outside the Great Wall, and not encourage or supply the volunteers to disturb 'Manchukuo'." However, the spokesman of the Japanese Embassy, ​​when talking about it, denied that Huang and Yoshizawa had discussed this matter, and the compromise conditions rumored the day before yesterday were also said to have been spread by the Japanese Embassy.

Representative Issues 116

Yesterday it was rumored that Japanese Minister Yoshizawa Akira would go north to serve as a representative when the time was right, but the spokesman of the embassy denied this yesterday. It is said that there has been no progress in this matter, and even if the time is right in the future, the Japanese minister will not go north to serve as a representative, because the nature of the solution is a military and local nature. It is also expected that the Chinese government will extremely avoid involving the Northeast issue, so this time the official diplomatic representative will only appoint a representative from the military, and if necessary, the embassy will send personnel to assist, just like the position of Japanese Minister Shigemitsu during the Shanghai ceasefire. As for the choice of military representative, there are still problems, because in terms of the Japanese military in North China, the commander of the Japanese army in North China, Nakamura, should be responsible, but in terms of war, the army that is fighting is the army of Commander Mutō, so Mutō should be responsible.

Interview with the Japanese Minister 117

Also, according to the interview with the Japanese consulate in this city yesterday, (1) Judging from the current situation, it is indeed possible for China and Japan to seek a buffer zone under mutual understanding. The purpose of the Japanese army is only to consolidate the security of the "Manchukuo" border. If the Chinese army can withdraw to the west line of the Luan River as Commander Mutō declared, and at the same time stop the activities of the volunteers, the Japanese army will definitely withdraw to the Great Wall and delineate a neutral zone, and no other conditions are required. (2) In the past two days, the war on the front line seems to have subsided slightly. In fact, the Japanese army does not need to occupy Peiping and Tianjin. Moreover, since Japan withdrew from the League of Nations, it has been diplomatically isolated. Occupying Peiping and Tianjin will inevitably cause international negotiations. This is not what Japan wants. Moreover, Japan's own economic strength and the current political situation do not allow the extension of the war against China. The reporter asked who is responsible for the negotiation matters between the Japanese Minister Yoshizawa in Shanghai and the Japanese Embassy in Peiping. He replied that Secretary Zhongshan is responsible. Military matters are the responsibility of Commander Nakamura of the Tianjin Garrison. If there are major matters, he will first consult with Commander Mutō by telegram, but there is no sign of diplomatic negotiations in Peiping now.

Wang Zhengting's Talk 118

Former Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, after arriving in Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday, gave a speech to a reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency, saying that it is indeed possible for the military in North China to start a ceasefire similar to that in Shanghai, but the distance from reality is still far. Because the Sino-Japanese issue is now that war cannot be mentioned, and peace cannot be mentioned either. It has become an international issue of an international nature. Therefore, the fundamental issue must be the rapid unity within our country to seek a solution. In any case, the vast lost territory, such as the three northeastern provinces, must never be given up. Wang said that more than 30 years have passed since the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-1895, and we have a great tendency to forget and do not know how to work hard and strengthen ourselves, so we have today. Let's see how Japan's policy of aggression is. Wang continued to mention US President Roosevelt's declaration, saying that it was very fair and great, but we still need to strengthen ourselves and never say that the Japanese army can be withdrawn because of Roosevelt's empty words. The way to strengthen ourselves should focus on productivity. There must be production, and the government and the people must cooperate. Because the government's responsibility is to protect the people, and the people's responsibility is to support the government. Therefore, the people have production and must rely on the government's protection. Otherwise, the people have no production and the government has no power to protect, then how can the country not perish? Wang believes that the Northeast issue cannot be resolved in just a few years, but we must have the determination to persist, that is, the determination not to sign any evidence of ceding the Northeast land, just like the Paris Peace Conference. If we do not sign any evidence, there is still hope for the recovery of the Northeast. This point is extremely important, and the people of the whole country must have this spirit. When Wang was speaking, he cited the Shandong Qingdao issue and France's Alsace-Lorraine issue as examples. The Shandong Qingdao issue lasted for eight years from the European War to 1922 before it was resolved. The provinces of Alsace and Lorraine were occupied by Germany for thirty to fifty years and were finally recovered by the French. Therefore, as long as the Northeast issue is not signed with a certificate of cession, it can eventually be recovered. Finally, Wang talked about the issue of compromise, believing that it is impossible, because the two sides have no Common Bases (low degree of solution), so there is no way to talk about compromise. May I ask if Japan can agree to withdraw its troops to the South Manchuria Railway line? The people of the country should not be able to sleep soundly just because there is an atmosphere of relaxation. We must know that the Japanese can still invade at any time.

International Radio Station and Mackay Company

Broadcast Began Yesterday Morning 119

The Sound is Still Clear

According to Xin Xin News Agency, the International Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications and the Mackay Wireless Telegraph Company have begun to broadcast. A reporter from Xin Xin News Agency went to the International Telecommunications Bureau yesterday morning to inquire. According to the staff of the bureau, the wireless communication between our country and the United States has already been broadcasting. This time, the communication with Mackay Company can be said to be a new route for communication between China and the United States. At a time when the international community is paying attention to the events in the Far East, the addition of this line is also beneficial to our country. The two sides started broadcasting at 3:00 a.m. yesterday, and the received sounds are still clear. It is also heard that this broadcast still uses the station's original motors and does not add any new ones.
