Various Circles Report Enemy Goods 121

Enemy Fish According to Yuan Dong News Agency, the Shanghai Fishery Inspection Committee for Enemy Goods recently received a secret report that two fish shops, Xie Xing and Tong Xing, were selling Dongkou dried fish, an enemy good. The committee immediately submitted it to the executive and supervisory committee for discussion, and decided that all the standing committee members would go to the two fish shops yesterday to seal them up. Xie Xing Store sealed up one large bunch and four large bags of Dongkou dried fish, and Tong Xing Store sealed up one large bunch and four large bags.

Enemy Paper The paper industry association sent a letter to the municipal chamber of commerce, which said: Dear Sir, the subordinate association recently received a secret letter from a gentleman, which briefly stated that China Fuxin Cigarette Company commissioned Fuhua Printing Company to print anti-Japanese posters (Pyramid cigarettes). The Iron Blood Group reported the matter, and your association (referring to our association) identified that they were indeed made of white cardboard printed with enemy goods. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce was requested to forward the letters separately to the Cigarette Factory Industry and the Color Printing Industry Trade Association to thoroughly investigate the case. After receiving the letter, the Color Printing Industry Association did not thoroughly investigate it. According to Fuhua Company's own confession that the Japanese goods paper and printing of this poster were all handled by itself, the association decided at a meeting at the beginning of April to report and announce the facts to the association (Color Printing Industry Association) and warn Fuhua for privately using enemy goods, etc. Unexpectedly, this resolution was put on hold. Later, due to the criticism from the outside world, it was inconvenient to put it on hold for a long time, so the previous resolution was changed, and only the printer (Fuhua) was ordered to publish an apology and pay a fine of 100 yuan. The punishment was inevitably too light, but once a bad example is set, the consequences will be endless. The following opinions are attached: (1) Fuhua Printing Company's purchase book clearly states that it received 22 reams of white cardboard from Fuxin Cigarette Company (Japanese goods anti-Japanese posters were printed with white cardboard), which shows that it was not handled by Fuhua. (2) It is absurd and ridiculous to privately use enemy goods for anti-Japanese posters, and it is a laughing stock to the world. (3) The fact of this case is that Fuxin Cigarette Company privately imported Japanese paper and entrusted Fuhua to print it. Now it is reversing the facts, avoiding the important and taking the light, and blaming Fuhua, so Fuxin Cigarette Company can still continue to import enemy goods. (4) It is heard from the staff of Fuhua Printing Company that this Japanese goods white cardboard was sold by four members of the paper industry association, but whether it is true or not remains to be thoroughly investigated. We have always admired your association's impartiality, so we specially wrote a secret report and requested you to quickly investigate and thoroughly investigate, etc. Upon receipt, according to this, since this case involves the subordinate association's colleagues, we have to conduct a thorough investigation. We will send the incoming letter to our industry inspection team for reply. According to the team's reply, they were commissioned to secretly investigate which company of the same industry sold the Japanese goods white cardboard of the anti-Japanese posters printed by Fuxin. A secret report letter was handed over to the team. After the team received the letter, they convened a meeting of cadres and staff on May 12 to discuss the secret letter. The following resolutions were made: (1) If it is as stated in the secret letter, the color printing industry association's handling of this case seems to have avoided the important and taken the light. In order to clarify the truth, it is proposed that you forward a letter to the municipal chamber of commerce, asking it to forward a letter to the color printing industry association, asking it to fully inform the handling of this case, so as to prevent external criticism. (2) It is proposed that you forward a letter to the municipal chamber of commerce, asking it to inquire with Fuxin Cigarette Company whether it issued materials (paper for printing posters) when printing anti-Japanese posters. If it issued materials, where did it buy this Japanese goods paper? (3) It is proposed that you forward a letter to the municipal chamber of commerce, asking it to inquire with Fuhua Printing Company where it bought the paper for printing anti-Japanese posters, or did Fuxin issue materials for printing? etc. The records are in the file. According to the previous reasons, we have recorded the case and replied. Please review and handle it, etc. According to this, the team's proposed method is still correct. For this reason, we have detailed the reasons and prepared a letter to be sent to you. Please review and reply, etc. This is addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The following is omitted.

Ji Zejin Talks

Reasons for the Failure of Chinese Tea 123

Adhering to Old Methods and Not Thinking About Improvement

Mixing Fish Eyes with Pearls Leads to Loss of Credibility

According to Xin Xin News Agency, in order to develop international trade, the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry convened a meeting of tea merchant representatives to discuss all methods to restore the inherent status of Chinese tea in the international arena. A reporter from Xin Xin News Agency interviewed Ji Zejin, the director of the guidance office of the bureau, yesterday. According to his talk, the reasons for the failure of Chinese tea in Australia in recent years and its remedial methods were explained in detail. The following is an excerpt: Ji said that tea is the largest category of Chinese goods shipped to Australia. In recent years, the tea market has also been occupied by Ceylon and Java. The reasons are nothing more than the following two: (1) Adhering to old methods and not thinking about improvement; (2) Dishonest behavior. According to 30 years ago, there was no other kind of tea in Australia. Later, because the customs found that the tea shipped from China was mixed with leaves and grass roots, and after adding flour paste and dry flushing into the water, there was no taste of tea at all. Only withered branches, rotten leaves and grass roots were seen. Australians greatly rejected Chinese tea, so tea from India and Java came in one fell swoop. To this day, Chinese tea has still failed to restore its credibility. This is the result of dishonest behavior. Secondly, Australians do not like plain tea (green tea such as Yū Qián Dragon Well and Maojian), but like black tea to take its golden color and strong aroma as the best product. Because Westerners drink tea, such as milk and white sugar, which is very different from the plain tea that Chinese people like. However, our country does not pay attention to it when transporting tea to Australia, and it does not know how to bake it with new methods, so it is very different from the preferences of Australians. Even if there is no mixing of grass roots, it may not be able to occupy the Australian market for a long time. Or there are those who change the method of baking tea to cater to the preferences of Australians, but after a long time, they use dishonest methods, such as baking tea with copper green, which is dangerous, or shipping Hui Long tea leaves to foreign countries and being discovered, which affects the reputation of tea merchants across the country. All of these are the reasons why Chinese tea is rejected in the Australian market. Furthermore, Australia imports about 3.5 million pounds of tea each year. To recover this interest, Chinese tea should pay attention to the following points: (1) Tea roasting must cater to the psychology and preferences of foreigners and use scientific methods. (2) Strictly prohibit tea merchants from dishonest behavior and unsanitary methods, mixing fragrant products, mixing fish eyes with pearls, and causing loss of overseas credibility. (3) The packaging must be firm and must not leak or lose its flavor. (4) Send more specialists to foreign countries for inspection to promote it. The above points require the cooperation of tea merchants across the country, and the promotion and guidance of the government, so the future of Chinese tea will not be difficult to restore its former glory.

Daily Newspaper Commentary

Japanese Cotton Mills in Shanghai 126

Mocking the Lack of Patriotism Among Chinese

Resulting in Incomplete Boycott of Goods

Therefore, Japanese Factories Have Bright Prospects

The Osaka Mainichi Shimbun reported on the 91st of this month that in April of this year, Military Attaché Rear Admiral Izumitsu was ordered to visit China to comfort naval officers and soldiers. At that time, the Japanese Emperor was very concerned about the current situation and future of Japanese spinning mills in China. After Rear Admiral Izumitsu's investigation, he reported in detail, and the Emperor approved as follows: "The total investment of Japanese cotton mills in China is estimated to be over 200 million yuan. Most of this investment is from individuals, so their prosperity or decline has a significant impact on the domestic financial world. The rise and fall of the Shanghai cotton mill industry is a very significant issue, whether viewed from the perspective of investment or employees. However, since the anti-Japanese movement, the industry has been at a crossroads. Recent reports from Shanghai indicate 'sluggish sales, increased inventory, and reduced work hours,' leading operators into dire straits. But from a historical perspective, we should strive to avoid such an outcome. The Japanese cotton mills in China are the oldest Japanese overseas investments. Naigaiwata set up a spinning factory in Shanghai in the 44th year of the Meiji era. Thanks to the painstaking management of President Kawamura Rihei, it has achieved today's success. As for Mitsui's investment in the Chinese cotton mill business, it is a joint venture with the British and not a completely independent Japanese enterprise. Over the past 20 years, its development has been no less than that of Naigaiwata. Since the Shanghai Incident, the factory has been closed. Although it has recently implemented appropriate production restrictions, there has been no improvement. There are two major reasons for this: (1) The adverse general social conditions. Domestic spinning benefits from the decline in exchange rates and the impact of reduced work hours, while various parts of China are suffering from the scourge of soldiers and bandits, leading to local desolation and reduced purchasing power. Even Chinese-owned cotton mills are reducing work hours, indicating the growing panic in the economic world. (2) The impact of the anti-Japanese movement. Although it is not obvious on the surface, Chinese goods, despite their low prices, have no sales unless Japanese goods are specially discounted compared to Chinese goods. Currently, the only Shanghai factory that remains closed is the Nichi-Ka Spinning Factory in Wusong. Other factories have also been closed for four or five months. Recently, work hours have been reduced one after another. Fortunately, the dedicated planning of the operators has enabled them to barely maintain operations. The reduction in work hours varies from factory to factory, with Kanegafuchi reducing by about 30%, Nichi-Ka by about 23%, and other companies by about 20% to 30%. This reduction in work hours is primarily to avoid financial pressure. In terms of production, the change of manufacturing materials avoids competition with Chinese cotton mills. Since then, the processing of products has yielded significant benefits, leading all factories to hold optimistic views. However, in the midst of the intense anti-Japanese sentiment, it is necessary to acknowledge the good phenomenon of Japanese products achieving considerable sales. This is because the Chinese seek only cheap goods and are not afraid of anti-Japanese groups. If the Chinese truly thoroughly boycott Japanese products, last year's products would have been impossible to dispose of. It is the Chinese people's inability to discover true patriotism and their pursuit of self-interest that allows our cotton mill industry to proceed without hindrance. In short, since the incident last year, one aspect is that our (Japanese) operators have been able to skillfully maintain operations, which is indeed a stroke of luck in misfortune. Now, the difficult hurdle of adverse conditions has been broken, and there is no need to worry in the future. 1. Protection through tariffs: The current ex-factory tax is lower than import duties. 2. The 400 million Chinese people, no matter how poor, must wear clothes, and Japanese goods are cheaper than other goods. This is evident in the fact that sales increased even during the peak of anti-Japanese sentiment. 3. Remaining operators strive for economical production, which can both compete with Chinese spinning and increase profits. In terms of technology, Chinese spinning is definitely inferior to Japanese spinning, as is efficiency. The same goes for factory equipment. For example, the completeness of the Naigaiwata and Nichi-Ka factories is something that Chinese factories cannot match. The Pudong factory of Nichi-Ka Spinning has 53,000 spinning machines and 500 looms. Its power generation equipment costs only 1.5 sen per kilowatt-hour. The complete water purification system and skilled workers give it an advantage over Chinese spinning in every aspect. Production costs are also lower than those of domestic factories, so the cost of raw materials is very favorable. Due to the above three reasons, the future of Japanese spinning in China is optimistic. The Japanese cotton mills in Qingdao have not been affected by the Shanghai Incident at all. The Manchurian Cotton Mill in Dalian and the Manchurian Spinning Mill in Liaoyang, as well as the Naigaiwata factory in Jinzhou, have achieved unprecedented success in recent years. As for the Tai An Spinning Mill in Hankou, although it is temporarily closed, it will soon resume operations."

British-American Tobacco Factories: The British-American Tobacco Company shortened working hours in various departments due to sluggish business, leading to disputes. After mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau, four temporary measures were agreed upon. Factories One and Two resumed work the day before yesterday. Aviation Patriotic Award

Office of the Committee Established 130

Wang Xiaolai and Six Others Elected as Standing Committee Members

A Westerner Destroys His Home to Save Our Country's Difficulties, Truly Commendable

The aggression of our country by the violent Japanese not only infuriates our own people, but also causes many foreigners living in China to feel indignant and righteously rise up. The story of [Miner Searle] Bates is a prime example. Now, Mr. Ackfu, a German in this city, is willing to destroy his home to save our country, which is even more commendable. On the 18th of this month, a grand tour was held at Ackfu Garden on the Great Western Road for this purpose. Cai Yuanpei, Xu Jingren, Zhu Ziqiao, Kong Yongzhi, Ye Yuhu, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yiting, Yu Qiaqing, Du Yuesheng, Chu Huiseng, Lin Kanghou, Guo Le, Xu Xinliu, Chen Zeqing, Lin Wojiang, Ye Fuxiao, Gui Yanfang, Chen Songyuan, Wang Yansong, Wen Hongen, Li Ting'an, Xu Peihuang, Pang Jingzhou, Liu Yunfang, Guo [illegible], Wang Xiaoying, Zou Wenshi, Li Dachao, Qin Tongli, Gu Jinghan, Liu Tiqun, Wang Junxuan, Bao Ruanxing, Fang Haike, Gao Tongyuan, Tan Bozhi, etc., as well as members of the press Zhang Zhuping, Yan Duhe, Zhu Yingpeng, Yan E'sheng, Wang Yingbin, Yu Kongwo, Jiang Jianhou, Zhou Shoujuan, etc., archaeologists Wu Hufan, Liu Gonglu, Qin Xiangchen, Westerners Coke, German Consulate Dormer, Jin, and Schawelson, German Righto, and others, and Hu Diyi and Lu Yuting, representatives of General Sun Dianying, a total of more than 300 people, unanimously praised a certain Westerner's enthusiasm for China. Chairman Wang Xiaolai briefly stated that a certain Westerner was willing to use his property to help China expand its aviation strength, and would also donate aircraft and military supplies worth millions, which should be a model for the Chinese people. He dared to present this great and passionate intention and the measures we have formulated to all of you present. Then Li Dachao, chief of the Municipal Government Section, reported on the progress. Subsequently, Mr. Xu Jingren, Mr. Cai Yuanpei, Mr. Zhu Ziqiao, and Mr. Chu Huiseng delivered speeches, emphasizing the great significance of the Aviation Patriotic Award and stating that it was different from ordinary lotteries. They hoped that the Chinese people would work hard to promote it and enthusiastically sell it. Those who immediately signed up for the cause were extremely enthusiastic, and the steps for implementation have been decided. Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Yu Qiaqing, Zhang Gongquan, Lin Kanghou, Li Dachao, Bao Junjian, and others were elected as standing committee members, and the persons in charge of each group were appointed. The office will be established immediately to actively prepare for it. The cause and the measures are recorded below.

Cause 131

Since the Japanese pirates invaded and plundered our Eastern Provinces, creating a puppet regime, it has been more than a year. Recently, they have intensified their efforts, gaining an inch and seeking a foot, trapping our Jehol and forcing our Great Wall. Looking out at Yan and Ji, there are already military operations. They are fulfilling their wild ambitions like a wild boar or a long snake, disturbing our rivers and seas, and watching our interior, which is by no means unexpected. This is truly an unprecedented national crisis for China. All citizens should rise up quickly and catch up. Those with strength should wield their weapons and advance, and those with wealth should destroy their homes to relieve the country's difficulties, holding the determination to die and seeking a new path for rebirth. If everyone unites with one heart, the national crisis can be resolved. Now, a certain Westerner, who has lived in our country for more than 30 years, regards China as his second homeland. Seeing the brutality of the Japanese army, he was inspired with a righteous spirit and was willing to donate his properties worth 1.5 million yuan, as well as the proceeds from the sale of his treasured antiques, to purchase aircraft and various military supplies. After investigation by our colleagues, the matter is true, and we admire his enthusiasm and friendship infinitely. If a Westerner can do this, how can we not strive? Therefore, following the example of the Xin Family Garden in this city, we will use real estate and antiques as prizes. After public discussion, we will use real estate and antiques as a foundation to issue an Aviation Patriotic Award of 1.2 million yuan, divided into 120,000 tickets, each costing 10 yuan, with an additional 12,000 bonus tickets. After returning the original price and all expenses, the remaining proceeds will be allocated to the Aviation Patriotic Fund and used to support the front lines. This approach will not only benefit our country's salvation but also comfort the Westerner's grand intention. It is a win-win situation and can be carried out without hindrance. All our compatriots should promote it and widely sell it, and can also use it as an example to become the backbone of national resistance. We have jointly initiated this with leaders from all walks of life and have presented it to the government for joint planning. All our compatriots should enthusiastically compete to purchase it and not let Bu Shi and Xian Gao be the only ones to stand out in the past. We express our sincerity and cannot help but look forward to it.

Measures 132

(1) The Shanghai community initiated the Aviation Patriotic Award and specially presented it to the government for issuance. These measures were formulated. (2) This award is specifically for raising funds to assist the government in strengthening air defense and purchasing aircraft and military supplies. It is named the Aviation Patriotic Award. (3) This award is temporary in nature and does not conflict with or duplicate the Aviation Highway Bonds issued by the central government. (4) The total amount of this award is 1.2 million yuan, with each ticket costing 10 yuan, totaling 120,000 tickets. An additional 10% of bonus tickets, totaling 12,000 tickets, will be added, for a total of 132,000 tickets. For every ten tickets purchased, one bonus ticket will be given. He is willing to estimate the lowest price, recovering half of the value, 750,000 yuan, and is even willing to donate 250,000 yuan from it to purchase aircraft and various military supplies to strengthen our country's air defense. Therefore, the Westerner actually receives only 500,000 yuan. (6) 300,000 yuan in cash will be allocated as the Aviation Patriotic Fund, and 100,000 yuan will be used as cash prizes. The allocation method is as follows: One special prize, a four-story Western-style building, covering an area of 8 mu, 4 fen, 7 li, and 1 hao, worth 450,000 yuan. One first prize, 2 mu, 4 fen, and 1 li of land, worth 50,000 yuan, antique art worth 30,000 yuan, and 20,000 yuan in cash, for a total of 60,000 yuan. The City Chamber of Commerce Again Requests

Cancellation of Telephone Price Increase 133

The Cost of New Equipment Cannot Be Passed on to Users

Regarding the telephone price increase, the City Chamber of Commerce sent another letter to the Shanghai Telephone Bureau yesterday, requesting its cancellation. The original text is recorded below: "Respectfully, on the 18th of this month, we received a joint letter from the Soap Industry, Pickled Vegetable Industry, Wax Candle Industry, and Alkali Industry Trade Associations, stating that the Shanghai Telephone Bureau's plan to increase prices for installing automatic telephone machines has been opposed by various trade associations, which requested that the Chamber of Commerce forward their request to the competent authorities to waive the price increase. The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications has replied, mainly stating that (1) the increased price is to pay for the purchase of equipment, (2) although the price is increased, it is still cheaper than in the concessions, and (3) the cost of calls to the concessions has increased. However, although there are difficulties for the government, the interests of users must also be taken into account to ensure fairness. This is explained below: (1) The cost of equipment is a one-time start-up expense, while telephone fees are a permanent recurring expense. If the government passes on a one-time start-up expense to users as a permanent recurring expense, it is not only inconsistent in nature but also a heavy burden, reducing the number of users, which contradicts the original intention of facilitating communication. This should be addressed by raising funds in another way, and it should not be taken from telephone fees. (2) The market in the concessions is more prosperous than in the Chinese areas. The original market in the Chinese areas is already not as good as in the concessions, and the "January 28th Incident" of last year has further weakened it. Efforts should be made to reduce the burden on citizens to gradually develop the market. If the market can be as prosperous as the concessions, or even surpass them, the benefits will be far more than several million yuan. We should plan for the long term and not just seek immediate gains and solve the current urgent problems. (3) Since there are more calls to the concessions, the fees collected are also higher. Any matter of communication requires both parties, and there can be no one-way communication. Even if income does not cover expenses, the difference must be limited. The focus should be on facilitating communication, not solely on calculating expenses. Furthermore, if telephone fees are too high, citizens will not be able to afford them and will inevitably unite nearby stores and residents to install a telephone together to save money, or borrow other people's telephones. There is already a practice in the concessions of charging a few coppers for each borrowed telephone call, which is very popular. From the perspective of social and economic trends, if the price increases, joint installation and borrowing will naturally become more and more common. Users may not have the convenience of self-installation, but the government's revenue will also decrease as a result. This will defeat the purpose of facilitating communication and repaying the cost of equipment. The above-mentioned matters should be discussed and decided by your Chamber of Commerce, and then forwarded for continued fee collection to maintain commerce, etc." The letter from the Timber Industry Trade Association also stated that "the Nanshi telephone company charges an additional four yuan per month. In this season of economic recession, businesses are unable to afford it. The various trade associations have requested the cancellation of the price increase, and everyone shares the same sentiment." The reasons for this matter are hereby presented in a letter, requesting that the Chamber of Commerce ask the Telephone Bureau to continue to charge the original price, and we are grateful. Although the request for waiving the price increase has been rejected by the Ministry, our Chamber of Commerce is a commercial organization, and the difficulties of merchants cannot be ignored. Although the Bureau is under the jurisdiction of the Ministry and has its own position, it should also plan for its own business from a broader perspective and give its sincere advice to the Ministry of Communications. If telephone fees are too high, several households will install one telephone together to save money, which is an obvious fact. Moreover, logically, the Bureau's installation of new machines is the same as the Wheel Bureau's addition of new wheels and the Road Bureau's addition of new cars. One is to add assets, and the other is to attract customers and expand business. Part of the cost can easily be recovered from this, while the other part should be supplemented by adding capital and shares. This is true of all commercial businesses, and the existing users cannot be forced to share the costs equally. It is appropriate to send a letter to the Bureau, requesting that it adopt the opinions of the public and make gentle representations to the Ministry of Communications, taking into account the difficulties of merchants, which is to promote business."

Japanese Ships Smuggling Refined Salt into Shanghai 134

Salt Authority Has Implemented Strict Enforcement

According to the Central News Agency, reliable sources have reported that recently, Japanese ships at the Yangshupu and Huangpu wharves have been smuggling refined salt into Shanghai from ports such as Dalian, Yingkou, Liaoning, and Qingdao. The salt is hidden in cargo at night and smuggled ashore. Because the smuggled refined salt is being smuggled by the Japanese, the police in charge have never interfered. Japanese soldiers patrol the wharves at night, and even if they see suspicious packages, they cannot go forward to inspect them. The amount smuggled each time is huge. Recently, the market has been flooded with refined salt, and it is often sold in small quantities of several packages, or mixed into table salt for sale, causing the salt tax department in the concessions to not sell even one catty. If this continues, the salt sales in the concessions will be completely taken over by this smuggled salt. If this continues, allowing it to be smuggled and sold privately, the national tax and commercial sales will inevitably be completely destroyed. Therefore, the salt authority has asked the concession and customs authorities to strictly assist in the enforcement and suppression to maintain the salt affairs.

Mr. Chen Zengguan, chairman of the association, considering the urgency of the foreign invasion and the peril of Tianjin and Beijing, and that all citizens should contribute their wealth to save the country, and that the performance of the 234th team of the solicitation team which he is in charge of is not good, had to seek other appropriate methods. Although the fellow traders of this association are in the poor class, they should also fulfill their corresponding obligations. If everyone is indifferent, the disaster of aggression will spread to the whole country. It must be known that after the country is destroyed, everyone's life and property will be lost together. If you want to protect the territory of the country, you must first seek the fulfillment of the air force, relying on the people's wealth to supplement the government's financial insufficiency. Now there are several questions for your decision: (1) Although most of the fellow traders in the solicitation team of this association have joined, the amount of donations is very small. Should we seek other methods? Resolved: Seek other methods. (2) The amount of donations and the collection procedures. Resolved: (A) Two thousand yuan. (B) All those who transport fresh pork in this city shall be charged two cents per head for aviation donations. (3) Collection location. Resolved: (A) Minsheng ship to Shanghai in Wusong. (B) Ship to Shanghai at Datong Dada Wharf. (4) Starting and stopping date of collection. Resolved: Starting from June 1st of this year, stop when two thousand yuan is collected. (5) Implementation method. Resolved: Send a letter to the Aviation Association Office to submit to the municipal government, please make a clear announcement, and inform the Seventh District General Office of the Public Security Bureau, the First District General Office, the One District One Branch, the Wusong Water Patrol Team, and Datong Dada Company to assist at any time. (6) The Northeast Refugee Donation collected on behalf of the banking sector. The Northeast Refugee Relief Association has already stated that it will end on April 26 this year and will no longer accept it. The banking sector has not stopped it. How should we negotiate? Resolved: (A) Inform the banking sector of the above in a letter. Stop collecting on the same day. (B) Correct the name of the previous donations. (C) If the banking sector needs to continue, it should be recognized by the banking sector itself. (D) Send a letter to the Aviation Association Office stating the reasons and submit it to the municipal government to order the pig industry association to stop collecting on the same day. (7) Upon receiving the notice from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, it is ready to join the Municipal Chamber of Commerce as a member. How should we handle it? Resolved: After all the membership procedures are completed, apply for joining in June. The meeting adjourned.

Inland River Shipping Labor and Management Request Both Sides to Ban Mechanized Sampans 141

Preventing Dangers and Striving for Safety

Since the commencement of operations by the Bianli Shipping Company on various inland river routes, the illegal infringement on their business by mechanized sampans from Shaoxing has persisted for several years, resulting in significant losses. Recently, the Construction Department of the Provincial Government investigated and confirmed that these mechanized sampans violated the province's single-line shipping regulations. They instructed the Songjiang County Government to issue a public notice banning all such sampans operating within the legal steamship routes of legitimate merchants. The remaining sampans were required to register with the County Government and were restricted from further construction, providing a fundamental solution. The Songjiang County Government has already instructed the water and land public security agencies to strictly enforce this ban. Recently, the Shanghai Inland River Shipping Trade Association and the Shanghai Inland River Shipping Labor Union have repeatedly received reports from their members regarding the infringement by these mechanized sampans. Considering the seriousness and widespread impact, the Association and the Union jointly submitted a request to the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department to promptly order strict enforcement to ensure the safety of the shipping industry. This demonstrates that the issue of illegal mechanized sampan operations has aroused opposition from both labor and management in the inland river shipping industry. The original request is excerpted as follows: "We respectfully submit this request regarding the illegal operation of mechanized sampans from Shaoxing, which endanger passengers and disrupt the routes licensed to our members, as well as the livelihoods of the ship's crew. We jointly request a thorough investigation and strict enforcement, without any leniency, in accordance with the provincial shipping regulations, to protect the business of legitimate merchants and the livelihoods of the ship's crew. Our Association and Union have recently received letters from the Shenping (Shanghai to Pinghu) members and ship's crew stating that all ships operated by the members on the Shanghai to Pinghu route, in addition to registering with the Ministry of Communications, have also applied to the Construction Bureau of each county for verification and forwarded to the Construction Department for approval in accordance with the temporary regulations for inland river vessel operating licenses issued by the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department. It has been observed that on the Shenping route, 70-80% consists of the vast Huangpu River, and 20-30% consists of small inland river ports. Recently, when the ship operators were operating the ships in the Huangpu River within the jurisdiction of Songjiang and Jinshan counties, they often encountered mechanized sampans from Shaoxing operating illegally. These sampans are of a crude construction, not complying with the principles of small steamships. The bow is lower than the stern, and the upper deck is heavier than the hull. Furthermore, they are operated by Shaoxing sampan boatmen who are not familiar with the navigation rules of steamships and lack safety equipment such as whistles. They often obstruct the passage of steamships and sometimes even collide with them. Although the ship operators exercise extreme caution, slowing down or even reversing to avoid collisions, the danger to the lives of the passengers on the mechanized sampans is imaginable. It is no wonder that there are occasional reports of capsizing and burning, resulting in injuries and deaths. If such incidents occur repeatedly, the ship operators will be unable to bear the responsibility that they should not bear. We request that the authorities be asked to ban them in accordance with the law. Furthermore, after the members sent personnel for detailed investigation, the matter is extremely serious. The sampan is simple and light. Even if our ships encounter them and slow down, they cannot resist the slight waves. Once a collision occurs in the Huangpu River, it is even more difficult to withstand. The sampan owners only care about making profits and disregard everything else. Small boats carry many passengers, and they drive recklessly in the Huangpu River. The danger is as reported by the ship operators. Furthermore, the mechanized sampan owners know that the hull does not comply with the principles of steamship construction, so they cannot apply for permits from the Ministry of Communications and the Construction Department. They dare to operate illegally without permits, cheaply infringing on the legitimate business of our members and the livelihoods of the ship's crew. This is extremely illegal. The matter concerns the vital interests of both labor and management. Therefore, we should jointly request the authorities to investigate and order strict enforcement throughout the province, in accordance with Article 7 of the temporary regulations for operating licenses, ordering them to stop operating, without any leniency, in accordance with the provincial shipping regulations, to protect the business of legitimate merchants and the livelihoods of the ship's crew, which is beneficial to both public welfare."

Chen Jizhang Accused of False Accusation Against Ye Liang 142

Ye Liang, a native of Nanxiang, the resident director and director of general affairs of the Shanghai National Arts Museum, previously dismissed Chen Jizhang, a native of Zhejiang and a document clerk of the museum, on March 30 for taking away the files and registers in custody without authorization, which was against his duties. Because Chen's address was 507 Racecourse Road in the Public Concession, he reported to the Laozha Police Station on the next day for investigation. On April 6, the museum suddenly sent a letter to the police station stating that the case had been settled through mediation outside the museum and requested that it not be proceeded with. However, Chen suddenly filed a complaint with the board of directors of the National Arts Museum and the municipal government against Ye Liang for various illegal acts, totaling five items and 24 sub-items. The main ones include falsely reporting public funds, forging resolutions, and requesting the municipal government to issue bonuses, etc. Chen also reported to the Bureau of Public Works that Ye Liang also served as an employee of the Finance Department of the Bureau of Public Works, so he repeatedly took the paper and stationery of the Finance Department to the National Arts Museum office in Bo Bo Lane, Luban Road for abuse. In addition, he also filed a statement with the Laozha Police Station stating that Ye's previous accusation that he had taken the documents privately was not true, but a false accusation, and requested that he be investigated according to the law. Such a three-pronged approach shows his psychology towards Ye. However, after the Municipal Government and the Bureau of Public Works separately investigated the accused articles, they did not find any criminal evidence as accused. The Bureau of Public Works also temporarily suspended Ye's position in the Finance Department of the Bureau when it began the investigation. After the investigation, since there was no fraudulent behavior, he was still ordered to resume his position. Ye was unwilling to give up after this blow. He especially requested the police station to indict Chen as a warning to those who falsely accuse him with prejudice. The police station then filed a false accusation against Chen. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court summoned both parties to the court. Qian Hongye, the criminal judge, tried the case. The police station lawyer Ru Baozhen stated the situation and said that the defendant Chen Jizhang had committed the crime of Article 180 of the Criminal Law and should be interrogated. Ye Liang also stated the reason for dismissing the defendant and the beginning and end of the false accusations against him by various agencies. When asked about the defendant's confession, the defendant said that the documents I took were all those that should not have been issued, but Ye forced them to be issued. Now these documents are still in the hands of a certain three directors of the National Arts Museum and can be verified in detail. Judge Qian then instructed the defendant to pay 300 yuan bail and reschedule the hearing in seven days.

Ye Jiwu Carried a Thousand Red Pills

Wang Shunxing Tried to Extort Unsuccessfully

Ye Jiwu, a 22-year-old native of Nanjing, who has been a machine worker at No. 17 Fuqing Lane, Gaochang Temple, yesterday morning at about 6:00, Ye purchased one thousand red pills at a red pill agency at No. 33 Ruihe Lane, Zilaihuo Street, French Concession, put them in a cloth bag, and hid them on his body, and took the French Chamber of Commerce Route 5 tram, intending to take it home immediately. Wang and others said, "Why are you pretending? Be clear, take it out." Ye knew that these people had bad intentions. However, because he was hiding drugs, he knew that it was difficult to deal with them. At that time, a Route 3 tram came, and Ye jumped on the tram to avoid them. Unexpectedly, Wang still chased him and jumped on the tram. When the tram arrived at Tanjiayingkou, Dadongmen, he grabbed Ye and shouted to the third post guard Wei Jinxiang, and took him to the responsible third station of the first district. When Director Jin interrogated him, Ye complained about the previous situation. When asked, Wang Shunxing confessed that he was 25 years old, a native of Zhenjiang, and lived at No. 176 Sanyuli, Taiping Bridge, French Concession. This morning, he came from the north of the city to the south to visit friends. He met Ye on the tram. At that time, he accidentally bumped into Ye's body, and a cloth bag of red pills fell out of Ye's body and was seen by him. However, Ye was still aggressive and scolded him for not bumping into him, which made him very angry, so he took him to the post police. Because Ye was carrying prohibited items privately, it was a violation of the prohibition, but Wang took the opportunity to extort money and made excuses to evade liability, which was also illegal. He was ordered to prepare a document and send it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau together with the red pills for investigation and punishment.

No fatal wounds were found on the surface of the body. The official then sat in court and questioned the deceased's wife, Yang Xu, the defendant Ding Genxi, the witness Xu Lihua, etc. about the circumstances of the fight. According to the deceased's wife, her husband was beaten to death by Ding Genxi's father, son, uncle, and nephews. The defendant confessed that the deceased's son spat cold water on his back first. He told him not to tie a bandage in the heat, but he ignored him and scolded him. He then hit him once, and his father, the deceased, came over and punched him in the right cheek before he could finish two sentences, so he fought back. The witness's confession was the same as the defendant's. The official checked the confession and ordered the forensic doctor to dissect the body again. After detailed examination, the result was that the deceased had heart disease before his death, and he died of paralysis due to insufficient heart strength after being beaten. The body was ordered to be collected by the deceased's brother Yang Rongzong after signing a guarantee. The defendant Ding Genxi was sent to the court by the police station for questioning. After the examination, the deceased's family sent the body to the Qingzhen Temple in accordance with the religious regulations, where the teacher chanted sutras, washed the body, and buried it. The defendant will be sent to the Second Special District Court for interrogation today.

Deshengxiang Store

Was Bombed Twice Last Night 149

Large Glass Shattered Again

Suspects Identified and Released

Deshengxiang Foreign Goods Cloth Store, Nos. 363 to 365 at the northeast corner of Zhengjia Muqiao Street, Fada Road, was opened by Beizaisun, a major merchant from Ningbo. In the middle of last month, a bomb was thrown into it, destroying a large glass window, fortunately without injuring anyone. Unexpectedly, it came for the second time last night at about 7:00. The bomb was still thrown in at the same place as last time. The explosion was very loud. The large glass, more than seven feet long, was shattered again. Various floral yarns and cloths displayed in the window were damaged a lot. At that time, passers-by all heard the sound and ran to avoid it, and the order on the road was in chaos. The Great Ziminzhong Police Station heard the alarm and immediately sent a large number of detectives to arrest them. Two suspects were arrested on the spot and taken to the police station. After the police chief questioned them in detail, he sent detectives to search the two suspects' homes and found no evidence, so he released them immediately. The police are now strictly pursuing the case.

Dada Steamship Company

Safe Arrival of the "Da Yu" Steamer in Shanghai 150

A report from the National News Agency states that the "Da Yu" steamer, belonging to the Da Da Steamship Company and operating on the Shanghai-Tongzhou route, was fully loaded with passengers and fresh goods on the 17th, departing from Tongzhou for Shanghai. However, while passing near Yao Port (about 30 miles from Tongzhou) that evening, it encountered dense fog and ran aground on a sandbar. The entire ship was thrown into a state of panic. After the fog cleared, the "Hong Da" steamer of the Da Tong Steamship Company happened to pass by and reported the incident to the water police, who dispatched a vessel for protection. Meanwhile, the fresh goods on the "Da Yu" were transferred to the "Hong Da" and transported to Shanghai to prevent spoilage due to delay. The "Da Yu" was finally freed the night before and arrived in Shanghai at 6:00 AM yesterday. Fortunately, there were no losses to the ship, cargo, or passengers.

Special Request from the First District United Association

Guaranteeing the Housing Lease Rights of Citizens 151

Submitted to the Municipal Party Department for Transfer to the Municipal Government for Approval

The First Special District Citizens' United Association of this city believes that the recently promulgated housing lease regulations by the Municipal Government could be exploited by landlords to infringe upon the lease rights of citizens. Therefore, they specially submitted a request to the Municipal Party Department yesterday, asking it to be forwarded to the Municipal Government for review and action. The original request stated: "Respectfully submitted, it has been observed that since the emergence of real estate speculation in the market, increasing rents and forced evictions have become prevalent. Lease rights are disregarded, causing hardship for citizens in both business and residence, and the social economy is declining daily. The customary practice of protecting tenants has not been valued by the courts, leading to declarations of provisional execution and rulings of provisional attachment, which have become weapons for those seeking to harm others. The situation in Shanghai is becoming increasingly precarious. The Municipal Government promulgated housing lease rules on April 21st of this year, which are most easily exploited by landlords, including (1) reclaiming for self-use, (2) property ownership changes, and (3) reconstruction approved by the Public Works Bureau. While reclaiming for self-use to terminate a lease is indeed a custom in Shanghai, it is limited to subletting surplus rooms. Even when approved by the court, a written guarantee must be provided that it will not be rented out again. This shows some protection of the tenant's rights. However, the current rules lack such restrictions, allowing even houses and city apartments specifically for rent to be reclaimed for self-use. The danger to tenants is evident. As for property ownership changes, they are easily fabricated by real estate speculators, given the lack of registration enforcement. Even if genuine, it fundamentally conflicts with Article 425 of the Civil Code, which states, 'Even if the lessor transfers ownership to a third party after delivering the leased property, the lease agreement continues to exist for the transferee.' This is because the rules stipulate that a fixed-term lease agreement, except for rent arrears of three months, only expires when reconstruction is approved by the Public Works Bureau. The Public Works Bureau's approval should have specific conditions, requiring the building to be at least twenty years old. Otherwise, the request for reconstruction cannot be rejected by the Public Works Bureau, even if it clearly knows that it harms public interests, due to the lack of legal basis. Therefore, it is necessary to stipulate in the rules that (1) reclaiming for self-use should be limited to renting out surplus rooms and not applicable to houses and city apartments specifically for rent, (2) Article 425 of the Civil Code should be strictly applied regarding property ownership changes, and (3) only buildings older than twenty years should be allowed to request reconstruction approval from the Public Works Bureau. Only with these stipulations can tenants have any degree of protection. The public should have a comprehensive understanding of the scope of implementation of these rules, and special districts should not be an exception. However, the provisions for the Public Security Bureau and the Public Works Bureau allow real estate speculators to circumvent the rules, which must also be noted. This matter concerns the protection of citizens' housing lease rights and the prosperity of the market. It is appropriate to submit this request for review and to urge the Municipal Government to take action, in accordance with the Party's principle of prioritizing the welfare of the people. This request is submitted to the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department."

Establishment of the Jiangsu Maritime Patrol Team in Wusong 152

Local News from Hengli

Discovery of Blood Fluke Germs 153

Attention for Those Visiting Qingyang Port

Dr. Zhou Deng, Director of the Health Department of the Municipal Council, received a report from the Lister Institute of Preventive Medicine stating that cattle in the Hengli area have been found to be infected with blood fluke disease (Schistosomiasis). Dr. Zhou Deng believes that, given this discovery, anyone bathing in the waters of Qingyang Port is at risk. Applying a disinfecting cream to the body before bathing can reduce the risk, but it is difficult to completely avoid it. Furthermore, those traveling by boat and staying near Hengli should pay close attention to their water usage. Water used for cooking is relatively safe because the germs are eliminated at higher temperatures. However, washing dishes may involve using river water, which requires special vigilance. The preventive measures are as follows: (1) Store the water collected for two days before use. (2) Add one gram of sodium bisulfate to every quart (one-quarter gallon) of drinking water. (3) Add a ten-thousandth solution of creosol to the water used for washing. Dogs can also contract the disease and transmit it to humans.

Death of Prominent Tea Merchant Zhu Baoyuan 161

Mr. Zhu Baoyuan, a prominent Shanghai merchant, was from Haining, Zhejiang. He came to Shanghai alone as a young man to engage in business. Through diligence, frugality, self-discipline, and perseverance, he built his enterprise over decades. He was also known for his generosity and public spirit, benefiting many in his hometown. Unfortunately, he passed away last month, causing widespread grief. Mr. Zhu was 54 years old. He had two sons and three daughters. The elder son, Yanqing, is the manager of the Zhenhe Tea Company, who was kidnapped last year. The younger son, Shunqing, was the head of the savings department at Zhengda Bank. Yonghe Trademark Objection

Original Verdict Upheld After Review 162

The trademark designs and colors of the Shanghai Yonghe Industrial Company are very similar to the previously registered trademark of the American Herdner Company. When the company applied for registration with the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, the Trademark Bureau repeatedly rejected the application. Recently, the company appealed against the contents of the Trademark Bureau's Objection Review Decision No. 196, requesting a review of the objection. The Trademark Bureau has now issued Objection Re-Review Decision No. 46, revoking the company's trademark in accordance with Article 3 of the Trademark Law. The main text of the decision upholds the review matters of Objection Review Decision No. 196. The reasons for the decision are lengthy and not included here.

Suicide Due to Disappointed Marriage Prospects 163

| Autopsy of Miao Fengyi's Body |

A young man named Miao Fengyi checked into Room 107 of the Qinghe Hotel at 188 Zhejiang Road the day before yesterday and committed suicide by taking poison. The police from the Light Gate Precinct received a report, dispatched Detective Wang Jiaju to transport the body to the Forensic Examination Office on Fellen Road, and notified the court for an autopsy. These details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that the deceased's original name was Miao Xingbao, from Jiangyin. He worked as a tea server at the Huadong Hotel on Shandong Road. His elderly mother and elder brother still reside in his hometown, where they are engaged in farming and live in poverty. His second elder brother, Guixiang, works at the Xinguanghua Light Bulb Factory on Bailebo Road in the French Concession. Miao, although over twenty years old, was still unmarried. Recently, a friend arranged a marriage for him, saying that a woman with a beautiful face could be married for a price of 200 yuan. Miao was very pleased to hear this and wrote a letter to his mother and brother, asking them to raise the money. However, he received a reply a few days ago stating that due to poor farming conditions, it was impossible to raise the money. Miao was very distressed by this news, and this was the reason for his suicide. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo Wei from the First Special District Local Court arrived to conduct an autopsy, confirming that he had died by taking poison before his death. The body was released to his brother, Miao Guixiang, who signed a statement agreeing to arrange for the coffin and burial.

Publishing World 167

▲ The Humanistic Monthly, Volume 4, Issue 4, Published

The Humanistic Monthly, published by the Humanistic Monthly Society on Lafayette Road, Shanghai, is highly respected by the academic community. It is reported that Volume 4, Issue 4 has been printed and released. The contents include Mr. Bai Jiao's "The History of the Student Movement and Student Unrest," which continues in this issue. Based on past facts, it comprehensively narrates the student movement and school unrest in concise language, especially the discussions on the May Fourth Movement, the May Thirtieth Movement, and the March 18th Movement, which are incomparable to superficial discussions. Anyone who wants to understand the causes and consequences of the student movement and school unrest over the past decade and its trends must read it. Mr. Jian Bing's translation of "The Innovation of Armaments" is by Liddell Hart, who experienced the European War, is knowledgeable in military science, and is now a famous military critic. This article describes the trend of modern new armaments. Reading it, one can understand the consumption of huge military expenditures in our country, while those responsible for armaments say that they are only enough to support a few days of combat, which is shameful, and that relying solely on crude and defeated military equipment and swords to kill enemies is insufficient to cope with the situation. Other articles include Mr. Wei Xian's "Miscellaneous Records of Zeng Yun, the Governor of Zhejiang," Yuan Tao Yu's "Records of Events in the Renyin Year," and Mr. Qian Banxiang's notes, which continue from the previous issue. "Reading Digest" and Mr. Hua Dingyi's introduction to "The Social Cultural Foundation" and Mr. Wang Zhaoshi's introduction to "British Political Organization" are all extremely valuable. The "Magazine Index" contains an exceptionally rich collection of materials. In addition to the Society's own sales, it is also available at Lifestyle, Crescent Moon, Modern, Juzi, Guanghua, Great East, Taidong, Author, Nanxin, Suxin, and major bookstores in other cities. It is reported that the annual subscription fee is three yuan domestic and four yuan eight jiao foreign, including postage. The first, second, and third volumes previously published are all available in cloth-bound hardcover editions.

▲ Publication of Library Forms and Supplies

The use of cards, forms, and specialized supplies in modern scientific management is an important part. The management of books, especially the need for cards and forms, is particularly important. Unfortunately, there has been no special book to provide detailed instructions, so that various libraries have not been able to fully utilize them. Now, Mr. Du Jiayou, a library expert, has edited the book "Library Forms and Supplies," which details the usage and styles of forms and supplies, totaling more than sixty types. It covers all library application forms and usages. It has been published and distributed by the Library Department of the Commercial Press on Niuzhuang Road, Shanghai. The China Library Service Society at No. 20 Museum Road also acts as an agent. Anyone who purchases a copy of the book will also receive a set of card samples.

▲ Modern Bookstore Wholesales National Publications

The Modern Bookstore on Fourth Road, Shanghai, in view of the numerous types of national periodicals, their different natures, and the varying distances of their publishing locations, as well as the limited personal abilities of readers and the difficulty in understanding the contents of each magazine, has specially opened a dedicated department after expanding its premises as the general distributor. It collects more than two hundred types of national periodicals and displays them earlier than other stores, allowing local readers to browse the contents of each magazine as much as possible. Since its implementation, readers have found it convenient. In order to further facilitate readers in other cities, the bookstore can subscribe on their behalf for those who wish to subscribe. The subscription price is the same as that of the publishing location. Readers in other cities who are unclear about the contents of the publications can write to the bookstore's postal department for inquiries. A list of national periodicals is printed and will be sent upon request.

With the foreign threat becoming increasingly urgent and the national crisis deepening, the Military Publishing House, in order to popularize national military common sense, has specially compiled a booklet entitled "National Practical Military Common Sense." The contents are divided into nine chapters, including the methods of offense and defense in infantry, cavalry, and artillery warfare, as well as protection against enemy aircraft bombings and poisonous gas, first aid and hygiene, and the use of first aid medicines. The language is concise and easy to remember, making it an essential book for students' military training and national self-defense in the era of war. Letter 173

To the Editor: I recently read in the Shanghai newspapers a news item about the transfer of ancient bronze Buddha statues from the Forbidden City to Beijing, saying that more than thirty ancient bronze Buddha statues, each more than three feet tall, made of a mixture of green and red bronze, and relics from the Tang and Song dynasties, were transported from Beijing to Shanghai and then reported to be transported to Beijing. It was said that they would be handed over to Director Wang for worship and responsible preservation. After investigation, what is said above is completely untrue. I hereby make a responsible statement, respectfully hoping that your newspaper will grant a correction. Sincerely, The Beijing Office of the Palace Museum in Beijing, May 18th.

National Humiliation Week Lecture: Mr. Wang Yunwu Speaks on January 28th 174

Speech given at the YMCA on May 13th

Since January 28th, I haven't gone anywhere to give a lecture. Today's lecture here is my first since January 28th. Why haven't I given a single lecture in such a long time? I feel that the decline in the physical development of the Chinese people is truly too severe. Other than a mouth, everything else is useless. The mouth can speak and sing high-sounding tunes, but the hands cannot do anything. Therefore, after January 28th, I have not participated in any lectures, except to make a resolution to do something.

Today, I came to the YMCA to speak because I really had a hard time refusing.

January 28th is not far from us in terms of time, and especially close in terms of space. So, if I tell you some facts, everyone knows them. If I tell you some theories, it will be close to singing high-sounding tunes. I will just talk about my feelings here.

Everyone knows very well that before January 28th, the people of Shanghai were all talking about resistance. But in the week before January 28th, because the disaster was imminent, many people wanted to seek temporary peace. On the night of January 28th, the municipal government finally surrendered to Japan. The Japanese consul expressed satisfaction. Many people simply thought that they could seek temporary peace, which is truly the most heartbreaking and shameful thing. I think it is not a disgrace for others to invade us with force. Our own lack of ambition is the greatest disgrace.

After the January 28th Incident broke out, everyone thought that the 19th Route Army could not resist, but the 19th Route Army was able to resist for more than a month! Also, everyone knows that the sacrifice of the Commercial Press after the outbreak of the January 28th Incident was very great. I think that the Commercial Press's sacrifice for the 19th Route Army, which was able to resist foreign insults, is still worthwhile, even though the loss was very great. The 19th Route Army's active resistance has great significance in national education. The sacrifice of the Commercial Press for this reason is even more effective than publishing 100,000 books to contribute to education and culture.

I often think that Chinese soldiers are the least afraid of death. Because the life of a Chinese person is very hard. Many people's houses are not much higher than graves. These people have no big difference between death and life, so Chinese soldiers are originally the least afraid of death when fighting. But because Chinese generals are too comfortable and too rich, they are reluctant to die. If you happen to encounter a few generals who don't want money and are not afraid of death, his subordinates will become an invincible elite force.

The purpose of the lectures held by the YMCA this week is to make people aware of national humiliation. In fact, we have so many national humiliations, how can we not know them? I think it is more useful to make people aware of their mistakes than to make them aware of shame.

I think our first big mistake is that what we say is too far from what we do. After the January 28th Incident occurred, all the shops in the city went on strike and only reopened after the ceasefire agreement was signed. They all posted a piece of paper at the door of the store, called "Opening for Business with Endured Pain." That's right! We are opening for business with endured pain! But what was the result? Some people changed "Opening for Business with Endured Pain" to "Opening for Business with Endured Happiness," which is very realistic. Most citizens are probably completely forgetting the pain they suffered before! Looking at all the improper pleasures in society after January 28th, how much has it decreased compared to before January 28th?

During the European War, the national lives of the participating countries were very hard. For the sake of long-term combat, not only were all unnecessary expenses eliminated as much as possible, but even two days of food were divided into three days for donation. At that time, Chinese students studying in Europe probably still remember the taste of the few slices of black bread they ate every day. Our country is now in a state of war, and our ability to defend ourselves is far inferior to that of the warring European countries at that time. However, the Chinese people, especially the citizens of Shanghai, have not reduced their enjoyment of peacetime at all. It's really inexplicable. Our country is in such danger. Even if we as citizens cannot actively do the work of saving the country, at least we must passively preserve a little vitality for the country. Unconscious consumption of materials is destroying the country's vitality. In addition, the physical strength of the people is also related to the country's vitality. After the European War, Germany's armaments were restricted by the Allied Powers, but the men, women, and children in their country paid special attention to physical training, preparing that once the country was at war with foreign countries, everyone could be a soldier. But what about us? We make all kinds of unconscious consumption in economic terms, and we only care about wasting our physical and mental strength. It is really heartbreaking and frightening to talk about.

The second mistake we need to know is that we have no direction. After September 18th, the people only knew how to sing high-sounding tunes, and the government only knew how to save face. A few days ago, the Big Evening News had an editorial saying that China now has not only no Yue Fei, but not even Qin Hui. The enemy is united as a nation and treats me according to a fixed direction. Our country wavers between peace and war. Not only is there no nationwide unified direction, but even a small group has divided opinions and conflicts before and after.

We have many mistakes, and these two can be considered the biggest. If we recall, since September 18th, our mistakes are countless.

We should recognize our mistakes and correct them thoroughly. The government and the people should not only care about face. We should determine the direction, unite against foreign countries, and then we can overcome the serious national crisis. Conversely, the darkness is increasing. Talking is also empty. (Recorded by Ye Wenxiong)

Japanese Hawkers Selling Counterfeit Powder

Taking Advantage to Rob Money 175

Steel Tooth Shop Couple Were Deceived

Police Have Stated They Will Not Prosecute

丨Sheng Xiyuan, Wang Awu, etc. Are Suspicious丨

At the inlaid tooth shop established by Zhang Yingming, a Ningbo native, at No. 110 North Zhejiang Road, this month on the 11th, several Japanese people accompanied by two Chinese people came to Zhang's place to hawk inlaid tooth white powder. After Zhang took it to the French Concession for inspection and found that the powder was actually flour, they took a car back to the shop. Unexpectedly, the Japanese and others had disappeared without a trace, and it was discovered that the iron box in the shop had been pried open, and 420 yuan in banknotes and silver dollars stored in the box had also been robbed. The police were then notified, and detectives Tao Afu and a Western detective were dispatched to investigate. Five bags of white powder were found. Because of its resemblance to morphine, they feared that there was a case of privately selling morphine, so Zhang Yingming, his wife Zhang Zhou, and Li Yutang were all detained and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation, awaiting verification of whether it was morphine before further investigation. Zhang Yingming and Zhang Zhou each paid a surety to be summoned at any time, and Li was still detained. Later, the police arrested the suspects, Wang Awu and Sheng Xiyuan, both natives of Shaoxing, and sent them to the court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning was the date for the continuation of the interrogation. Zhang Yingming hired lawyer Shen Xingxia to appear in court as his representative. Police lawyer Li Zhishan then stated the case, saying that during the adjournment period, the police had sent the white powder to the Bureau of Public Works' Sanitation Department for testing. The result was that it was identified as flour, not morphine. Therefore, they are now not prosecuting Zhang Yingming, Zhang Zhou, and Li Yutang. However, Wang Awu and Sheng Xiyuan are suspected of colluding with the Japanese Yoshimoto, Nakamura, Nishitani, etc. to rob Zhang Yingming of 420 yuan in silver dollars, and one of the Japanese has been arrested by the police and sent to the Japanese Consulate for investigation. There are still accomplices in this case who have not been apprehended, so they requested a further postponement. Judge Wu Tingqi ordered the Zhang couple and Li Yutang to step down as witnesses. Zhang Yingming testified that on that day, two Japanese people and Sheng Xiyuan and one person who was on the run came to sell five bags of inlaid tooth powder. I took them to the French Concession for inspection and found that they were actually flour. When I returned to the shop, the iron box had been pried open, and 300 yuan in silver and 120 yuan in banknotes had also been robbed. At that time, my wife Zhou saw it with her own eyes, etc. Zhang Zhou and apprentice Zeng Difu also came to the police station to testify, proving that on that day, they saw Sheng Xiyuan and a Japanese person coming to talk in the shop. Not long after, Sheng left first, and the Japanese immediately broke into the back, obtained an iron tool, broke the iron box, and robbed the silver dollars before escaping, etc. When questioned, Sheng Xiyuan confessed that he went with the Japanese Yoshimoto, Nakamura, and Nishitani, etc., but he was not present during the robbery. Afterwards, Yoshimoto distributed 56 yuan to him, and he temporarily stored 23 yuan with Wang Awu, etc. Judge Wu verified the confession and ordered Wang and Sheng to be detained, Li Yutang to pay a surety to be summoned at any time, and Zhang Yingming to remain on his original bail, awaiting a further interrogation on the 26th.
