The Most Precise Dial 178

— Li Yuanqing

For tuning dials used on broadcasting or transmitting machines, even the slightest movement can prevent a stable oscillation. Therefore, the indicated points on the dial must be very accurate.

The indicator diagram discussed in this article is made using the principle of a vernier scale. Paste a black paper of considerable size on the back of the dial. Use white powder to draw ten grids on the black paper. The size of each grid is one-tenth smaller than the grids on the original dial. The total distance of ten grids is only equal to the position of nine grids on the original dial (as shown in Figure C). When using, pay attention to the small numbers when the upper and lower lines merge, which are the required decimal points. As shown in Figure A, it is 18.7 degrees, and Figure B is 38.8 degrees.

Semi-AC Single-Tube Radio 179

— Kai

AC radios have now replaced DC radios, but in terms of sound clarity, AC radios are ultimately inferior to DC radios, especially in single-tube radios. However, easy management and low cost are the advantages of AC radios. If we combine the advantages of both, we can make a semi-AC radio with very few changes in the DC aspect. Other parts are still powered by batteries, which can have the above-mentioned advantages.

Of the electricity used by DC radios, the A battery is the most expensive, and the B battery is more economical. Therefore, the A battery is first discarded. Now, we use a side-heated vacuum tube and use a doorbell transformer to light the filament, which can save costs. The B battery is still used to maintain the clarity of the sound quality. Doorbell transformers usually output around 10 watts. The secondary coil has different voltages, ranging from 3 volts to 8 volts or 4 volts to 12 volts, with a current of 1 ampere. To meet the needs of the vacuum tube used, the secondary coil can be removed and rewound according to the following method.

Suppose the vacuum tube used is 227, its filament voltage is 2.5 volts, and the current is 1.75 amperes. If the original secondary coil of the transformer has 285 turns and its maximum output voltage is 8 volts, then it should be rewound to 89 turns, as shown in the following formula: 丨

Once the number of turns is obtained, the transformer was originally 1 ampere, so it is advisable to wind two wires in parallel, which can obtain 2 amperes. The circuit can still use the ordinary regenerative force type as shown in the figure.

Simple Lightning Protection Device 180

— Xu Runsen

Summer has arrived, the weather is humid and hot, and there are often thunderstorms. If high antennas are affected by lightning strikes, they will inevitably damage radio components. Therefore, attention should be paid to lightning arresters. The following devices can be installed at very low cost. It is worth trying. (1) This figure only requires a single knife switch. Connect it according to the diagram. During thunderstorms, close it downwards, and the atmospheric electricity will directly enter the ground.

(2) Use a double knife switch. Connect it according to the diagram. During thunderstorms, close it downwards. The antenna is completely grounded and isolated from the radio, which is the safest.

(3) Use a light switch and a plug. Install them according to the above diagram. When listening to the radio, just insert the plug into the plug. During thunderstorms, unplug the plug and close the switch above.

(4) You can use a burnt-out filament vacuum tube or an old light bulb. Solder the ground wire to the two legs of the vacuum tube GP, and then connect it to the radio to form a lightning arrester. The atmospheric electricity voltage is extremely high and can fly through the vacuum, directly connecting to the ground wire.

High-Voltage Vacuum Tube 181

— Li

At present, the filament voltage of wireless radio vacuum tubes is mostly from 1 volt to 6 volts, and the filament power is supplied by transformers. However, manufacturing transformers is one of the difficult problems, because if it is too large, it will take up too much space, and if it is too small, it will easily heat up and burn out. This often causes those who purchase wireless radios to pay an unexpected repair fee.

Several years ago, people in Europe thought about manufacturing high-voltage vacuum tubes that do not require transformers. Now it has been successful. Its detection, amplification, oscillation, rectification, and all effects are completely the same as the vacuum tubes currently in use. However, its filament voltage is 110 or 200 volts, which can be directly connected to household power, greatly simplifying the manufacturing of radios.

Triode

Double-Screen Rectifier Tube 182

Its filament is somewhat like the filament in an electric light bulb, but it doesn't glow white-hot, so the heat is relatively low. Even if there are voltage fluctuations in the circuit, no noise will be generated, the sound will not be affected, and there will be no humming. Its lifespan is also greatly increased because, for those used with 110 volts, the filament temperature is only around 900 degrees Celsius, while ordinary 4-volt ones are around 1200 degrees, making them easily damaged.

The filament is inside a cylinder made of a rare earth material. The outside of the cylinder is coated with a layer of metal oxide. The control grid is a metal wire wound into a spiral shape, and the screen grid is not a sheet but a very fine metal mesh.

The rectifier tube has two or four pairs of rectifiers. Those made into a Wheatstone bridge circuit can output extremely smooth direct current, which can be used to supply vacuum tubes that require higher screen grid voltage. Specially made "high-voltage tubes" can be used. When using 110 volts, the output is above 310 volts. Another advantage of this type of vacuum tube is that it can also use direct current, so the radios made can be used no matter whether the power source is direct current or alternating current. It can be called one of the recent major inventions in the radio industry.

How to Check the Standard Time of the Observatory 183

— Yunzhen

Now that you have a radio, you certainly want to get the most accurate time. The Xujiahui Observatory broadcasts standard time via telegraph every day at one minute before 11:00 AM and 5:00 PM. Don't think that this telegraph is too fast to listen to, because even if you haven't learned Morse code, you can understand it.

The standard time telegraph broadcast starts every day at 10:55 AM and 4:55 PM.

From 55 minutes to 56 minutes and 50 seconds, send ::丨 once every two seconds. From 57 minutes and 0 seconds, send 丨:丨 once every two seconds. Until 57 minutes and 54 seconds, send ::::. The last dot is exactly 58 minutes and 0 seconds.

After that, you can hear five 丨·. The first 丨· that is heard is 58 minutes and 10 seconds, and the second 丨· is 20 seconds. And so on, until 58 minutes and 54 seconds, send …. The last dot is exactly 59 minutes and 0 seconds.

After that, there are five 丨丨·. When the first 丨丨· is sent, it is exactly 59 minutes and 10 seconds, and the second 丨丨· is 20 seconds. All the way to 59 minutes and 54 seconds, send …. The last dot is exactly 11:00 AM or 5:00 PM.

This telegraph has three wavelengths on a broadcast radio:

One is at 1450 K·C, slightly shorter than R·U·O·K.

One is around 970 K·C, next to the Zhejiang Province broadcasting wave.

One is around 550 K·C, even longer than the Tianjin broadcast wavelength.

Radio Operation Instructions (2) 184

— Tigan

(2) Method of Responding to Radio Telegrams

(1) Before communication between stations A and B, the transmitting station A should call the call sign of the receiving and transmitting station B three times, then send the 丨: (DE) signal and the call sign of its own station three times.

(2) Before mutual responses between stations A and B, the wavelengths of the two stations must be those monitored by each other.

(3) When the called station B hears it, it should immediately call the call sign of station A three times, then send the 丨… (DE) signal and the call sign of its own station three times. If station B is ready to receive the telegram, it can send the 丨·丨 (K) or 丨丨:丨 (GS) signal. If an explanation is needed, it should be stated briefly at that time.

(4) If the called station B cannot receive the message, it should send the ·丨… signal instead of the 丨·丨 signal in item 3, and add a number to indicate how long to wait. If it is necessary to wait for more than ten minutes, it should be explained briefly at that time.

(5) If station A needs to send multiple telegrams in succession due to having many reports, it should explain it briefly to station B and obtain its permission.

(6) When station B permits station A's request, it should add a number and the 丨·丨 signal to indicate the number of copies that can be received in succession.

(7) For telegrams with more than 100 characters, it should be limited to one copy, and multiple copies should not be sent in succession.

(8) For telegrams with many characters, they should be divided into paragraphs. Each paragraph should be 50 characters for clear text, and 20 characters for cipher and affixed words. After each paragraph is sent, a :丨: question mark should be added to ask if it has been received correctly. If it is correct, reply with the 丨·丨 signal, and then the sending station can continue to send the next paragraph.

(9) After the telegram has been sent, the ·丨·丨· signal should be sent, and the sending station call sign and the 丨·丨 signal should be added to notify the other party that the station has finished sending.

(10) If the receiving station receives the telegram correctly, it should immediately use the ·丨· (R) signal, followed by the telegram number, the sending station call sign, the 丨… (DE) signal, and its own station call sign to indicate that the telegram has been received correctly.

(11) If the receiving station continues to receive more than two telegrams and verifies that they are correct, it should use the ·丨· signal, followed by the number of telegrams, the numbers of the previous and subsequent copies, the sending station call sign, the 丨… signal, and its own station call sign to indicate that the reception is correct.

(12) If the work of both stations A and B is completed, each station should send the …丨·丨 signal and its own station call sign to declare that their work is completed. (To be continued)

▲ Radio Receivers During the Plum Rain Season. The most vulnerable time for radio receivers is during the plum rain season. Recently, there have been consecutive days of thunderstorms, and the weather has entered the moldy season. Upon inspection of the radio, the circuits are intricate and there are many parts. Once invaded by moisture, they will either mold and rot or fall off. The most important parts are the loop antenna and the frame antenna, which can become moldy, or the resistors and capacitors can corrode. As a result, the radio may make strange noises, or it may be completely silent, and various other inaudible phenomena may occur. Furthermore, being struck by lightning can make the radio sound inferior. The radio repair department of the Yada Company, located at 25 Renji Road in this city, has received a large number of requests for radio repairs due to consecutive days of thunderstorms. They are now hiring more specialists to engage in repairs, ensuring prompt delivery. The company's low prices and excellent repairs are particularly praised by all sectors of society.

▲ New Building of the Research Institute to be Completed in November

Yang Xingfo, Vice President of the Central Research Institute, returned to Shanghai from Beijing yesterday morning. There was originally a plan to move universities in Beijing and Tianjin south, but now that the call for peace in the north is high and the war may be coming to an end, those universities will not move south. Japanese Bandits Aim to Annex

The Shanghai University Student Federation telegraphed Minister He in Beijing yesterday, saying, "Respectfully to Minister He in Beijing, Jianjian, the enemy troops have captured Shixia and crossed the Luan River. Beijing and Tianjin are in danger like eggs stacked on top of each other. Japanese bandits aim to annex and have devised numerous schemes. If Beijing and Tianjin are not defended in the end, the impact on the final outcome of the Sino-Japanese issue will be enormous. For the current plan, the only option is to urgently deploy heavy troops to defend Beijing and Tianjin, and with the spirit of immediate action, fight a desperate battle with no retreat. Rather be a broken jade than a complete tile. Sincerely, we earnestly plead for your consideration. The Shanghai University Student Federation."

Methods for Soliciting Paintings for the Municipal Health Exhibition 194

The Public Scale Standard Has Been Changed to the City Scale

The Use of Domestic Goods for Painting is the Principle

The Shanghai Municipal Health Education Exhibition, jointly organized by the Municipal Health Bureau and the Education Bureau, had previously formulated six regulations for soliciting health paintings created by students from various schools. Regarding the regulation on the size of the drawing paper, it is now known that the public scale standard has been changed to the city scale. As for the drawing paper, if it is absolutely necessary, the principle of using domestic paper should still be followed. All other regulations remain the same.

Tongji University's 26th Anniversary 195

Wusong Tongji University has been in operation for 26 years, with excellent management and outstanding achievements. It can be called one of the famous universities in the country. The 25th anniversary last year was not held because everything had not yet returned to its original state after the January 28th Incident. This year marks the 26th anniversary, and it is scheduled to hold a commemorative ceremony on the 20th of this month. In the afternoon, there will be a sports meet and a variety show. It is also reported that there will be a reception for German, Austrian, and Swiss students and Tongji alumni the following day.

Re-election of the Education Association in the Eleventh District 196

The term of office of the Shanghai Eleventh District Education Association has expired. A general meeting was held at 4:00 PM on May 17th at No. 9, Zhenru Jinan Literary and Science Museum, to re-elect the executive committee. Wang Jiren was publicly elected as chairman, and Chen Tianyu was the recorder. Cao Peizi, sent by the Municipal Party Department, Ding Shoutang, sent by the Pioneer Education Association, and Zheng Hongnian, sent by the Education Association, attended the meeting to provide guidance. As a result of the election, Zheng Baoning, Tang Tonghou, Chen Zhongfu, Yang Yu, and Fen Yao Zhenduo were elected as members of the association's executive committee, and Wang Jiren and Wang Deheng were elected as alternate members. They were immediately sworn into office. The main resolutions passed by the general assembly are excerpted as follows: (1) The Literacy Movement with One Yuan case; (2) The case of improving rural production using scientific methods; (3) The case of planning a simple mobile library; (4) The case of the school subject competition in this district; (5) The mass amateur sports case; (6) The suggestion to the Municipal Education Association to strive for uniform treatment for teachers in municipal schools. In addition, at the executive committee meeting held at 3:00 PM the following afternoon, Zheng Baoning was appointed as the standing executive director, Chen Zhongfu was appointed as the director of general affairs, Tang Tonghou was appointed as the director of publicity, Yang Yufen was appointed as the director of research, Yao Zhenduo was appointed as the director of investigation, and paid staff were hired to assist with the affairs. There were considerable methods for the cases entrusted by the general assembly, as well as the funds, equipment, and community night schools.

Those who have been selected will be used first. In addition, due to the lack of performance basis, it is inevitable that some talents will be missed. Therefore, a preliminary election meeting will be held on the afternoon of May 27th (Saturday). Those who reside in Shanghai, are amateur track and field athletes, and are not listed in the table below, and wish to take the test, can register with the YMCA from now on.

(2) The selection method will be completely based on the merits of the results. The number of people participating in the restriction will not be the standard. Fortunately, all sectors of society pay attention.

First Day of the Inter-School Athletic Meet

Excellent Performances in 100m and 200m 205

▲200m Preliminary Round Sets New Record of 23.6 Seconds

▲Yesterday, Shanghai Middle School Dominated Field Events, Guanghua Excelled in Track Events

▲Finals to Continue This Afternoon from 1 PM

The Shanghai Inter-School Athletic Federation's 4th Track and Field Meet was held at the China Athletic Field starting at 1:30 PM yesterday. The weather was unfavorable, and the spectators were sparse. It started with drizzle and then turned into heavy rain, greatly diminishing the atmosphere of the meet. The athletes and staff were soaked. The performances were quite outstanding, especially in the 100m and 200m, where there was an abundance of talent and fierce competition. In the 200m preliminary round, Jiang Jiaxian and Dong Chu both set a new meet record of 23.6 seconds, which was not easy. In yesterday's finals, Shanghai Middle School dominated the field events with 10 points, while Guanghua excelled in track events with 7 points. In the women's division, the situation was even between Guanghua, Shanghai Middle School, and Jinan University. Currently, Guanghua leads with 17 points. Details are recorded below.

Miscellaneous Notes on Various Competitions 206

▲Outstanding Sprint Performances: Liu Jiaxian (Minli), Dong Yinchu (Guanghua), and Huang Feilong (Jinan) are outstanding talents in sprinting. In the 100m preliminary round, they all won with 11.8 seconds. Li Songnian of Daxia is also strong. The finals today will surely be a fierce battle, and the outcome is hard to predict. In the 200m preliminary round, Liu Jiaxian and Dong Yinchu both set a new record of 23.6 seconds. Huang Feilong was knocked down by Liu. It's also hard to predict who will win in today's finals.

Women's 50m First Place: Shi Peili (Guanghua) (Photo by Li Zunyong)

▲Tense Long Jump Competition: The strength of each competitor in the long jump was quite even. Wang Jusheng of Shanghai Middle School won the championship with 5.59 meters. Lin Shihua was second with 5.55 meters, Gong Hong third with 5.54 meters, and Hu Bao fourth with 5.53 meters. The differences were minimal.

▲Satisfactory Discus Performance: Liu Jiayu's victory in the discus was not unexpected. However, due to the rain and slippery ground, and the discus being contaminated with cement, it was difficult to exert force. The result of 30.39 meters was still somewhat lacking. The results of the second, third, and fourth places were quite far apart.

All Hands on Deck Today 212

丨Mass Meeting at the China Baseball Field丨

(1) Times vs. People's Voice...3:15 PM

(3) Shen Bao vs. Current Affairs...5:15 PM

Since the opening of the Shanghai six major newspaper editorial department inter-departmental football league, three matches have been played, with full spirit and strong interest. The battle between Current Affairs News and People's Voice the other day, fought in mud and water up to the ankles, was especially grand. Today is the third day of the single round-robin schedule. The soldiers and generals of the six newspapers are all out in force, and the battle will surely be even more exciting than before. Details are recorded below.

▲Today's Schedule

Competing Teams Start Time Location Referee

(1) Times vs. People's Voice 3:15 PM Baseball Field Shen Huichun

(2) Morning News vs. News 4:15 PM Baseball Field Shen Huichun

(3) Shen Bao vs. Current Affairs 5:15 PM Baseball Field Zhang Yi

The matches will start on time. It is hoped that the team members of each newspaper will arrive at the field in uniform in advance and await orders. It is also hoped that each team will appoint one linesman.

▲Rain or Shine

There were thunderstorms in the past two days, and the ball field was flooded with several inches of water, which goes without saying. Observing the weather, there is still little hope of clearing up today, but in order to express determination and courage, regardless of the situation, it is necessary to kick it out clearly. The words "weak scholar" have always been linked together, which feels uncomfortable, and even has an insulting meaning. Scholars are not necessarily weak, and the weak are not necessarily scholars. No matter if it thunders or rains, today we will definitely not believe in three things and not take four basins, and we must make it clear. As for borrowing the baseball field, we have already made an agreement with Mr. Zhou Jiaqi, so there is no problem.

▲Visitor Information

Today's competition will naturally attract many colleagues and workers from various newspapers to cheer, and even more wives and children will come to comfort and support. In order to maintain order, please take a seat on the grandstand. Non-newspaper fans are also requested to do the same. In short, except for substitutes, no one is allowed to cross the wire fence.

▲Warning to the Cabinet

During the previous two games, the reporter discovered two amusing anecdotes: (1) The cabinet premier of a certain reporter put on a stern face and said to his black lacquer bench, "You already have a group of children, don't follow them and make a fuss. These things are done by young lads." (2) A Suzhou nanny said to his young master, "Young master, the madam told me to tell you not to play football, and to go see a movie together." These were all witnessed by the reporter at the City First Sports Field, and it seems that reporters are only allowed to do "indoor work" and not "outdoor work," which is a great mistake. Considering that this is the first time, we will allow them to make amends for their crimes. Today is the day for self-renewal. If such incidents occur again, the football committee of each newspaper will impeach them and will not tolerate them.

Davis Cup North American Zone Final

U.S. Wins Two Singles Against Canada 213

Special Article

General Overview of Education in Various European Countries (3) 214

— Recorded by Lu Bingqian

IV. China's Educational Problems (1) "Teacher Training": Germany has very strict qualifications for teachers, requiring a university degree. Previously, graduates of normal schools had to attend university for further study to improve their level, making it difficult to become a teacher. University graduates first work as assistant teachers for three or four years, and even fifteen years, before they can take on a position. China is not like that. University students are unwilling to become primary school teachers, let alone assistant teachers. There is a deep sense of hierarchy. In foreign countries, as long as it is their interest, education is their lifelong career. I used to advocate that primary and secondary school teachers should have the same training, and there should be no distinction in training. At the time, I thought it was a dream, but now Germany is implementing it, and I know that it is not just an ideal. Secondly, teacher experience is also very important. England does not pay much attention to teachers' knowledge, but focuses on practical training. A normal school student usually has practical experience before graduating. In Russia, the number of schools has developed very rapidly in recent years. The number of illiterate people used to be around 85%, but now it is only 11% or 12%. Almost all the people in the country can read, except for some parts of Siberia. Because of the development of schools, there is a shortage of teachers. They first set up schools, and when there are not enough teachers, they appoint those who can read and teach, and then train them while they are teaching, such as organizing research groups, so that everyone has the opportunity to continue their studies during their service. China's current situation requires an emergency solution, and Russia is a good example. Just now, Director Pan said that only 30% of the children in Shanghai are enrolled in schools, while 60% are not. The same is true in Nanjing. There are so few schools, and children naturally do not have many opportunities to go to school. This phenomenon is very dangerous. It is naturally difficult to ask for progress in Chinese education. I think we can set up more schools now, and it is not too late to seek progress when the number of schools has reached a considerable level. (2) "Child Care": European countries pay much attention to child care, probably because after the war, there were too many deaths and the fertility rate decreased. At the same time, children's bodies also degenerated, so they had to pay attention to this point. Vienna, Austria, is even more thorough in its child care. It pays attention before a child is even born. They divide the city into several districts, and each district has several nurses who are responsible for investigating each family or trying to change their environment. When a woman is about to give birth, they notify the factory to approve leave for her.

Spring and Autumn Annals

The Realization of "Short Action Tales" 215

— Zhan Lu

Storytellers refer to stories about "battling rogues," "stealing the alliance book," or "breaking the Copper Net Formation"—the kind of martial arts novels called "short action tales." The meaning of "short action" is different from the elaborate armor and flowing robes of the "Romance of the Three Kingdoms" or "The Story of Yue Fei." These tales are best suited to the working-class, farmer-laborer society. The further one gets from the city, the better the business for short action tales. When someone speaks of a punch or a kick, scaling walls using skill, or the plum blossom stance showing its ability, it's guaranteed that the short-action-clad listeners will have their eyebrows twitching, their faces tensing and relaxing, making all sorts of comical expressions.

Since Shandong Chairman Han Fuqu has issued a document seeking talent, inviting extraordinary individuals from all directions who know how to scale walls, capture, and apply pressure points. I imagine that "under a heavy reward, there must be brave men," and perhaps there are already many strange and bizarre figures on the roads of Shandong coming to be Justice Han's Huang Tianba. However, without a staged battle, without demonstrating their amazing abilities in front of the masses, is there a possibility that the characters in short action tales could actually come to life? That remains a question.

Although Shandong has not set up a fighting stage, one is about to appear in Hong Kong. The former director of the Guangdong-Guangxi National Arts Hall, Cai Yigong, is a renowned disciple of Wang Yinlin. He knows how to wield swords and weapons, and also how to separate hands from body, not to mention techniques like pressure point strikes. Merchants and gentry in Hong Kong admire his martial arts prowess and want to invite him to Hong Kong to promote national martial arts at this time of national crisis. Furthermore, they plan to build an ancient plum blossom pole fighting stage in Shatin, New Territories, to welcome participants from all walks of life. The plum blossom poles will be made purely of large cedar trees, standing twelve feet high. First, 547 large cedar poles will be planted in the ground, each one foot apart, arranged in a plum blossom pattern, with five poles forming a flower, for a total of 108 flowers on the stage. Under the stage, weapons such as knives, spears, swords, and halberds will be displayed. There will be no wooden ladder; one must rely purely on skill to ascend and descend. Without superior national martial arts, one cannot ascend this ancient plum blossom pole fighting stage. Upon seeing this record, all sorts of "Golden Platform Tales" and "Seven Heroes and Five Gallants" short action tales seem to have a greater possibility of becoming reality.

Promoting national martial arts is not to be criticized, but when enemy planes and cannons can do as they please, merely promoting national martial arts may be too slow to be of any use! While promoting the martial arts of the old era, one must also invent the lethal weapons of the new era. If the Big Sword Corps were all-powerful on the battlefield, would the enemy be able to run rampant to this extent? In my opinion, the lethal weapons of the new era are even more necessary and applicable than the martial arts of the old era.

A Shared Biography of "Ah San" and "Ah Si" 216

— Yang Yusheng

Since Ah Dai and Ah Er went out to sing lotus flower ballads together and never returned, only Ah San and Ah Si remained. Speaking of Ah San's qualifications, he can truly be considered an old Shanghai hand. More than sixty years ago, when Shanghai was still a desolate land, Ah San followed the Westerners to Shanghai to do the work of clearing the wilderness. At that time, Shanghai was certainly not as prosperous and convenient as it is today. After working hard, the Westerners wanted to find a chair to sit on and rest, but they couldn't, so they always shouted "I Say" at the top of their lungs. Ah San would inexplicably run up to them, and they would pat him on the back, meaning they wanted him to face the ground and squat down, and thus a "man-made chair" was successfully created. It is said that Westerners spent most of their time reading newspapers and smoking on this man-made chair.

Since Ah San had made such a contribution, and because he had no home to return to, the Westerners treated him specially. At that time, Ah Si was truly ignorant, daring to make trouble for the Westerners and spout wild talk about killing Westerners. So the Westerners used Ah San to discipline Ah Si. To this day, Ah San still stands at the crossroads with an armed belt, slapping Ah Si in the face a few times to relieve boredom when he is happy, which is really impressive!

It is said that the troubled Ah Si is an unsuccessful descendant of a once-prominent family. His ancestors were hereditary land brokers who specialized in doing business with foreigners. The land they "sold out" in their hands amounted to no less than tens of millions of square miles. However, the Westerners did not particularly favor this dedicated "tiger slayer." On the contrary, they said that he had a cheap bone and no sense of national identity, and was not as favored as Ah San, so his family's situation gradually declined. Until Ah Si's generation, it might be the last generation, the Westerners were so cunning that they could use force to seize land, and they did not need brokers to solicit business, so Ah Si's hereditary title was declared abolished. After this blow, Ah Si became depressed and increasingly gluttonous and lazy, and became wilted. The Westerners originally said that he was a sick man, and their encroachment became even more severe, so he became even more afraid, running away at the sight of the Westerners' shadows. It is a pity that he originally suffered from twenty-three years of pulmonary tuberculosis, and now he is suffering from poverty and disease, both internally and externally, and he is so haggard that he is simply unrecognizable. However, his nature is very proud. He saw that Zhuge was called "Crouching Dragon," so he compared himself to a "Sleeping Lion." Of course, when the lion is sleeping, any animal can bully him, but once he wakes up, no one can be his opponent. Ah Si's ambition is evident here. However, Ah Si himself is probably not sure when this sleeping lion will wake up, so Ah Si is still an Ah Si, until he is eliminated!

Two Interesting Anecdotes of Wang Tieshan 217

— Zheng Yimei

Wang Hu (Tieshan) was indeed a worthy and honest official of his generation. The people of the country unanimously mourned his death. I heard anecdotes about him from friends at gatherings, and I have selected two of the most interesting to record, perhaps for excellent conversation after tea and wine.

Hu maintained personal frugality. Even after becoming the Governor of Jiangsu Province, he still maintained the original character of a poor scholar, wearing simple cloth clothes without any luxury. He often went out without attendants, walking on foot. Only when his feet were sore and tired did he hire a rickshaw as a substitute. Sometimes, when the rickshaw puller asked for too high a price, he often hesitated to spend a few copper coins and would stagger home. He also adhered to a policy of cost-cutting regarding household expenses, saving to the point where it was impossible to save any further. His wife still personally drew water from the well and raised ducks and chickens, not shirking from hardship. One day, he suddenly returned home and saw his wife feeding white rice to the chicks. He was very unhappy and rebuked his wife, saying, "Why are you feeding the chickens white rice instead of bran?" His wife disagreed, and a quarrel erupted immediately. He carried his remaining anger and went outside to buy bran, but unexpectedly, he could only find white rice and no bran at all. Only then did he realize that he had been rigid and wrong to blame his wife. He quickly apologized to his wife, and she forgave him with a smile.

He did not prepare many dishes for his meals, saying, "Since it is eating, rice should be the main focus, and dishes should be secondary. Wealthy families often have a variety of dishes and delicacies served at every meal, which deviates from the original intention of eating." His favorite dish was steamed crucian carp, with ham, winter mushrooms, scallions, ginger, and lard on top, which he regarded as an unparalleled delicacy. During festivals, he would definitely eat this to comfort himself. Someone advised him that if he liked crucian carp so much, why not cook it often? He replied, "The delicacies of the world should be savored and enjoyed gradually. If you devour them all at once, that is what crude people do. Moreover, killing a life every day for the sake of satisfying one's appetite is not permitted by Confucianism." A certain subordinate knew that he had a fondness for crucian carp and specially bought several large crucian carp to curry favor with him, keeping them in a magnetic pot, where they were still actively swimming. Unexpectedly, when he saw them, he not only did not express welcome but refused to accept them. The subordinate insisted, and he said, "I appreciate your kindness, but it would be impolite to refuse. In that case, I will hang a few of the fish you gave me in the hall so that the guests will know that you gave them." The subordinate was greatly ashamed and hurriedly took the fish and fled.

A Day Trip to Suzhou on May 7th 218

— Lin Zhipeng

I've long heard that the beauty of Suzhou surpasses that of Jiangnan, and I've dreamed of exploring it many times. Temples half-emerge from clusters of green trees, pagodas stand deep where white clouds rest. Sitting by the mountain corner is more enjoyable as the wind blows, and the trip is not yet satisfying as the sun sets over the city walls. As a traveler, it's hard to allow myself the leisure of Mao, a bright moon illuminates my return journey.

Visiting the Lion Grove Garden with Mr. Cheng Shengyang 219

Strange rocks are exquisitely connected by winding paths, and the entire garden's flowers and trees reflect the red curtains. Clear streams and willows bring spring tenderness, and pear blossoms in the small courtyard are hidden in the mist. Climbing to the high pavilion, the spirit naturally strengthens, but the dream of galloping in the Central Plains becomes empty. Don't ask about the beacon fires reaching the sky, just immerse yourself in the painting.

Long Novel

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 220

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seven: Severing Affection with Harsh Words and Grieving Behind Closed Doors; Shouldering Righteousness and Discussing Matters with Wine

But he said that he was determined not to talk to you, saying it would be useless because you wouldn't listen to him anyway, so why waste his breath? Because of this, I said to him, let me relay these words to you, so that the two brothers don't lose their harmony over these words. Ji Zhi was speechless after hearing these words and kept his head down in silence. Later, Mrs. Gan said, "You don't have to make things difficult. Once these words are said, they're done. As long as you're willing to break off contact with Miss Lao, your brother won't blame you for the past. Besides, he already asked us to refuse her visits more than a month ago. If you hadn't made an appointment with her at the milk tea shop yesterday, you wouldn't have had any contact. Frankly, isn't this all trouble you brought on yourself? I'm not good at speaking, so I only have these few words. Listen if you want, don't listen if you don't want, this is all I have to say, think about it yourself." With that, she threw away the short cigarette butt in her hand, lit another cigarette, and took a deep puff. She raised her head, leaned back in her chair, with a slight smile. Ji Zhi sat in the hall for a long, long time, and suddenly, as if he had thought of something, he stood up, bowed to Mrs. Gan, and said, "Sister-in-law, please take care of everything. I've realized it now, and I'll do as you say." Mrs. Gan exhaled a puff of smoke and smiled at him. Ji Zhi saw that things were not good and pleaded again and again. Mrs. Gan stared at him for a long time, seeing that he had softened, and then smiled, "If you have indeed realized it, I will naturally help you. Don't worry, I will definitely not make things difficult for you." Ji Zhi saw that his sister-in-law's attitude was very sincere when she said this, and he didn't think she would tease him. Moreover, his sister-in-law could make most of the decisions regarding his brother's affairs. What his sister-in-law said was even more effective than what his brother said, so he could rest assured. However, because of such a serious warning, he softened completely. As soon as he returned from the office, he retreated into his study. For a whole week, he didn't dare to take a step outside. Miss Lao was a little anxious. What had she done to offend him? After their meeting that day, why did he suddenly stop seeing her? Could it be that the words he spoke to her that day were all lies? As he thought about it, this question deepened. He followed his previous routine, going to the street to wait for Ji Zhi at around four o'clock, so that they could talk on the road. (75)

In the morning session, general sentiment was wary of continued selling pressure from No. 46 and No. 32 from the previous day, so the various listings were hesitant, rising and falling without consistency. Later, when unified taxes were auctioned, the surge to cover short positions raised prices by 3-4 cents. Although No. 46 sold this month's salt tax contracts, they still rose by 6 cents due to insufficient supply. The disparity between supply and demand for long-term salt tax contracts was absolute, leading to a sudden rebound, with a sharp increase of over 1 dollar, showing a strong trend. The next session saw a consistent increase of several cents. The 20th customs bond uniquely increased by as much as 8 cents. In the afternoon opening, the rising momentum still had remaining force, and the various listings continued to rise by 1 to 4 cents. Starting with the long-term 20th customs bond, a surge of selling suddenly turned the market negative, reversing to fall by 2-3 to 5-6 cents. The close then saw a consistent retreat of 1-2 to 7-8 cents, with only the long-term salt tax still up by 1 cent. The result was that, except for the current-month demobilization bonds, which fell by 1 and a half cents, the rest continued to rise by 1-2 to 8-9 cents, with a trend of large increases and decreases and considerable turbulence. However, No. 46 sold current-month salt tax contracts in significant quantities near the settlement date, indicating that they must have physical goods. Based on this deduction, even if there is a rising momentum in the future, it will be greatly affected. Silk and Tea: Continued Records of Spring Silkworms in Jiangsu and Zhejiang 234

(Changzhou) According to news from the surrounding villages, due to economic reasons, ant rearing has decreased. In the Huainan, Daning, and Fengdong villages, the amount of silkworms raised by silkworm farmers is only 40% of last year's amount. Ant rearing is smoother in Yangqi, Daixi, Xueyan Bridge, and Maji Shantou. The weather is mild, and silkworm ants are developing smoothly. The early group has finished the third molt and are ready for leaf feeding, while the next group is feeding leaves during the third molt. The late group has just begun the third molt. In recent days, there have been thunderstorms, wind, hail, and sultry weather, and the silkworm ants have experienced delayed leaf feeding due to sleep deprivation and diarrhea. If the weather turns sunny and smooth in about ten days, a good silkworm harvest can be expected.

(Xinchang) Also a Zhejiang province-owned area for improving silkworm rearing. Many farmers are hatching improved varieties, and the silkworm ants are developing well, with the Huangze area being the best. The early group has already entered the major molt, the next group is also feeding leaves during the third molt, and the late silkworms are also in the third molt. In the recent days, thunderstorms and sultry weather have caused problems. The foreign silkworm varieties only have minor sleep deprivation and lotus leaf symptoms, while the local silkworm varieties have experienced diarrhea, yellow water, rotten bellies, and stiff deaths. Silkworm farmers are deeply worried. Mulberry leaves are sold at 4-5 cents per Dan.

Free Talk

Public Opinion on the Sino-Soviet Railway Issue 243

— Shi Yi

The rumor that Russia is going to sell the Sino-Soviet Railway has caused an uproar in public opinion. Not only have commentators in newspapers denounced the Russians for being unfriendly, but some "labor unions" and "public organizations" have also issued statements of opposition, as if the fall of the Northeast and the imminent danger to Tianjin and Beiping are of no concern, and only the sale of the Sino-Soviet Railway is more important than a bomb dropping on their heads.

The Sino-Soviet Railway is the best fuse for arguments between the Japanese monkeys and the old bear. We are hoping that they will really start fighting, which will agitate the monkeys. Then we can reach out and conveniently "recover the Northeast". Unexpectedly, this bear is extremely cunning. It doesn't want to argue with anyone. If the monkeys want its Sino-Soviet Railway, it will simply sell it off, leaving the monkeys with nothing to argue about. This has upset us Chinese who are waiting for its forceful intervention, and we are loudly protesting:

"Aren't you, old bear, opposed to imperialism? Why are you compromising with imperialism again!"

Even the words that we once used to scold "red imperialism" are now being denied. Chinese people have this skill.

But even commentators who oppose the sale of the Sino-Soviet Railway say: "Although our Northeast is currently under the control of Japanese imperialism, being trampled by violence, there will eventually be a final reckoning, and one day the property will be returned to its original owner." The evidence is that our government is still "resisting while negotiating." And there is also a "long-term resistance plan." Since the entire Northeast is now merely "lodged outside the home," and the puppet state is coming forward to buy the Sino-Soviet Railway, it will still be ours in the future. So what does it matter whether Russia sells it or not? If it is really sold, it can even save us a sum of "railway redemption funds." Wouldn't that be cheaper? Then isn't it strange that public opinion is so agitated!

Heavenly Secrets 244

— Jingzi

It is difficult to speak, and even more difficult to listen. Because it is difficult to speak, language becomes more and more obscure day by day, so that it makes you understand and not understand at the same time, just like reading the Tui Bei Tu and Shao Bing Ge, only later can you fully understand. Because it is difficult to listen, most people simply choose not to listen, but only open their eyes wide to look. Because although the Tui Bei Tu and Shao Bing Ge are difficult to understand, there will always be facts to explain them afterward.

Not long ago, someone said: "Because we cannot fight, we must resist; because we cannot make peace, we must negotiate." The words were beautifully spoken, sophisticated, and considerate, satisfying both those who advocate war and those who oppose it, those who advocate peace and those who oppose it. But whether to fight or to make peace makes people more and more confused. Phrases such as "long-term resistance," "negotiate while resisting," or "we will resist when the enemy comes" all contain endless articles in a few simple words. Because there are articles, they are obscure. This is the transformation of language into the Tui Bei Tu.

Recently, someone said again:

"The current situation is like a lane with more than ten houses. The first two have already caught fire, and three or four are about to catch fire. If we do not quickly isolate them, the rest will burn together."

Also said:

"Someone is pressing my neck with a sharp knife, not killing me immediately, but forcing me to fall. Now that I have not fallen, there is still a chance to save the situation. Once I fall, it will be beyond salvation."

This is of course another Tui Bei Tu with a lot of articles. If the words were spoken like this: "The first two houses are on fire, quickly get the fire engine to pump water and put out the fire;" or "Someone is pressing my neck with a sharp knife, and I will return it with a sharp knife. Now that I have not fallen, I will fight to the death," then it would be dull and there would be no articles to write. And if the listeners were to ask: "Why only demolish the walls and not use fire engines to put out the fire?" "Why do I sit and wait for death when someone is pressing me with a sharp knife?" This would naturally be a stupid person who doesn't know how to listen.

The way to read the Tui Bei Tu is not to speculate from the literal meaning itself, but to understand and verify it from the facts outside the words. So, what are the facts outside of demolishing the walls? First, the "traitors" and "rumors" are compromising with Japan; second, "enemy," "rebel," and other overly stimulating words are all being avoided; third, the military situation in North China has temporarily ended, and the entire line has entered a state of truce; fourth, after ××× arrived in Peiping, people's hearts were greatly stabilized, and everyone believed that there must be a proper solution. Enough, just looking at these four points, can't we also glimpse the heavenly secrets of the Tui Bei Tu?

However, glimpsing heavenly secrets is ultimately not an easy task. Most of the ignorant people can only listen to "fate" in the dark until the walls have been demolished before they know. What happens when they know? After all, people cannot pick up stones and break the sky. Naturally, this is precisely the wonderful use of "heavenly secrets"!

Outside the French Park 245

— Tao Tao

1. One morning in late spring, the whole city was awakened by the sounds of workers at work. On the sidewalk outside the French Park, two former subjects of the Russian Empire, a woman in her forties with a child of seven or eight, were walking quietly. She was always so calm, as if nothing was worth her attention.

The child walking in front suddenly turned around!

"Mom! Can we take a look at the park before we go?"

She didn't answer him, as if agreeing and not agreeing. But her child couldn't resist, stomping his feet and clinging to the cement railing, looking greedily at the inside of the park like a hungry eagle chasing after food.

"Mom! Deer! Deer!"

She also leaned against the railing and looked inside.

Like the rest of the White Russian women, her face was always stern, without a hint of a smile. She wore a floral cloth on her head, and her wide coat wrapped around two breasts like gourds. She used to be a noblewoman, and few people would believe it if you said it. Her child wore an old peaked cap and a set of clothes made from his father's old clothes, looking very pitiful. But if it weren't for that cursed revolution, he would have been a nobleman, a hereditary title, worthy of respect. But now everything is over, everything has been destroyed by the thugs in their country. ...

Looking inside, two large deer and one small deer were confined inside a wire fence, walking so listlessly. She thought:

"Ah! This is really pitiful!"

She looked again. Under the shade of the trees, a couple was talking softly and walking, the man gently holding the woman's waist, face to face.

"Ah! ......"

The child was watching a girl put a doll on the ground, so he didn't pay attention to his mother's sigh.

She suddenly fell into deep thought.

When she married Dakov in Paris in 1918, the priest who officiated at the wedding also said that this young couple was happy. At that time, she certainly didn't expect to end up in the situation she was in now. At that time, they believed that they would be able to drive the thugs out of the country in a short period of time and return home safely. Who knew that now they were drifting to Shanghai, and the country was still occupied by thugs. ...

"Ah! What can be done? We have drifted to Shanghai." She thought to herself, "Ricky's father, for the sake of life, abandoned the dignity of a prince and carried a grinding machine to sharpen foreign knives for people. Ah! What a shameful thing!"

"Ah! Spring is on them!" She couldn't help sighing.

"Ricky! Go back!"

"Um! ......"

He obviously had his eye on that doll, on that little girl's doll.

She looked at the little girl again:

The little girl was wearing a dress with a large collar, and a butterfly was tied in her hair. She scooped the sand into a tin box, and next to her was a doll, which was exactly what Ricky wanted.

"Bansen! Come!"

"Ah! Louis."

"Did you bring the foreign gun?"

"I brought it."

"......"

"........"

She turned around to look at Ricky, and she sighed again:

"Spring is on them!"

She pulled Ricky forward, but Ricky was still looking inside the park. She suddenly thought of her husband sharpening foreign knives for people, and she sighed again:

"Spring is on the wealthy!"

"Mom! ......" Ricky didn't understand what she meant and stared at her with wide eyes.

"Ah, child," she said, "when you grow up, you must return to the motherland. Even living with those thugs is good!"

Random Notes from the Qu Cottage 246

— Zizhan

(30) A Study of Kong Yiji

When I first read Lu Xun's "Kong Yiji," it seemed to depict a "bookish fool" from my hometown. In the local dialect of Hunan, the term "bookish fool" always refers to a clumsy and unsuccessful scholar. This is still a respectful term; with a slight mockery, they are directly called "tung oil can" or "broken chamber pot." When I first started school, I also learned to write "Shang Da Ren Kong Yiji" in my tracing book. The schoolmaster was a type of bookish fool, so he was a bit higher than Kong Yiji. After reading Kong Yiji, I used this nickname to refer to the waste of the eight-legged essayist class, viewing the terms bookish fool, tung oil can, and broken chamber pot as far more vulgar and more brilliant. Recently, I borrowed a note from my friend Mr. Zhigang's reading manual, copying a passage from the Ming Dynasty scholar Ye Sheng's Shui Dong Diary: "Shang Da Ren, Qiu Yiji. Hua San Qian, Qi Shi Er Shi. Er Xiao Sheng, Ba Jiu Zi. Jia Zuo Ren, Ke Zhi Li. Shang Shi You Shan Shui, Zhong Ren Zuo Zhu Lin. Wang Sheng Zi You Xing, Ping Zi Ben Liu Xin. Wang Zi Qu Qiu Xian, Dan Cheng Ru Jiu Tian. Shan Zhong Fang Qi Ri, Shi Shang Yi Qian Nian. The above sentences are what all children in rural schools use when imitating calligraphy. They all start with this, which is called tracing in red. Everyone passes it on and learns it, almost all over the country, but no one knows what it means. Some say that it only takes simple strokes, with no other meaning; others say that the meaning is clear and understandable, and that it has a source." The Qiu Yiji mentioned here is Kong Yiji. Zi's name is Qiu, which needs no explanation. Ming people learned this tracing book from the beginning, but did not know where the language came from. In the Dunhuang anthology, there is a passage in the education category that says: "Shang Da Ren, Qiu Yiji. Hua San Qian, Qi Shi Er. Nv Xiao Sheng, Ba Jiu Zi. Niu Yang Wan, Yue She Tun. (The editor notes in the margin: The following handwriting is blurred and unreadable.)" It can be seen that this tracing formula is very old, probably dating back to before the Tang and Song Dynasties? And Kong Yiji will be immortal.

Carrot Top 247

— Jules Renaru, translated by Lin Quzuo

New Year's Day (continued)

Carrot Top: Just be patient for a moment, Mom will be done soon.

Mrs. Lepic: It's very literary, but the handwriting is too bad, I can't read it at all.

"Okay, Dad," Carrot Top said quickly, "now it's your turn."

As Carrot Top stood straight, waiting for his answer, Mr. Lepic read the letter over and over again, scrutinizing it for a long time, and making a few "Ah! Ah!" sounds as usual. Then he put the letter on the table.

This letter is now useless, its mission is over. It now belongs to everyone. Anyone can look at it, take it. Sister Ernestine and brother Felix took it in turn, looking for some spelling errors. Carrot Top should use a different pen nib here so that others can see it more clearly. Then they returned the letter to him.

He turned the letter over and over, smiling stupidly, as if asking:

"Does anyone want this letter?"

Finally, he stuffed it back into his hat.

At this time, Mrs. Lepic distributed New Year's gifts to the children. Sister Ernestine got a big doll, and brother Felix got a box of lead soldiers ready to fight.

"I bought you something unexpected," Mrs. Lepic said to Carrot Top.

Carrot Top: Ah, is that so!

Mrs. Lepic: Why do you say: Ah, is that so! Since you knew, then I don't need to give it to you.

Carrot Top: If I knew, then I would never see God.

He raised his hand high and said solemnly. Mrs. Lepic opened the cupboard. Carrot Top gasped. She reached into the top of the cupboard, all the way to her shoulders, slowly and mysteriously, and took out a sugar-glazed pipe made of brown sugar.

Carrot Top's face shone with joy without hesitation. He knew what to do now. Soon, he would be smoking in front of his parents, under the envious eyes of his brother Felix and sister Ernestine (but no one can have everything!). He only pinched the sugar-glazed pipe with two fingers, bent over, and tilted his head to the left a little. He pursed his lips into a circle, tightened his cheeks, sucked hard, and made a sound.

Then, he looked up and pretended to exhale a big mouthful of smoke:

"This pipe is very good," he said, "it's very smooth."

Back and Forth

The two little Lepics and Miss Lepic returned from vacation. When jumping out of the public carriage, when he saw his relatives from afar, Carrot Top thought:

"Should I run to them at this time?"

He hesitated:

"It's still a little early, I'll run out of breath, and I shouldn't show it too much."

He hesitated further:

"I'll start running to them from here............, no, start from there..............."

He asked himself some questions:

"When should I take off my hat? Which of the two should I hug and kiss first?"

But brother Felix and sister Ernestine had already rushed ahead of him to divide up the affectionate caresses. When Carrot Top arrived, there was almost nothing left.

"Why, you're so big, and you still call Mr. Lepic 'Dad'?" Mrs. Lepic said, "You should say 'My Father' to people and shake hands with him, that's how a man should be." (To be continued)

Talking Points

Tacit Understanding 248

— Niu

In the past, the format of letters often ended with words such as "tacit understanding," or "clear understanding," etc. At the time, I didn't pay much attention to it, thinking it was just a habit in writing letters. Now, looking at the newspapers, I suddenly realized the wonderful use of tacit understanding.

Tacit understanding means heart-to-heart, which also means mutual understanding. Your heart is known to me, and my difficulties are also understood by you. To go a step further, your heart is not only known, but can also agree to my difficulties; not only understood, but can also be followed. However, for the sake of face, or fear of others gossiping, it is not convenient to show anything clearly. Speaking of men and women, our love has reached full maturity, but because of parental opposition and the ridicule of others, we can live together, but we are embarrassed to officially exchange accessories and hold a wedding ceremony. This is an example of tacit understanding.

I once heard old hands at seduction and theft say that a wife is not as good as a concubine, a concubine is not as good as a prostitute, and a prostitute is not as good as theft. Secret affairs are the most interesting. Therefore, people abandon their wives and specialize in private affairs with other people's adulteresses. The so-called privately sold salt becomes more popular the more it is banned. If you look at the facts, this woman has been raped, her reputation has been ruined, her innocence has been stained. Even if you go to court and file a lawsuit, it will be useless. You might as well marry this rapist. But in fact, it must not be so dirty. She is still a good, pure woman.

Such a shameful thing, if it comes from someone with no personality or no prestige, then we don't need to say anything more. But if it is after all, a young lady from a noble family, raped, and it just ends quietly, then I'm afraid it will be difficult to do.

Now, people who read newspapers are at a very high level. They often don't look at the front, but prefer to find the reverse. They not only want to look at the reverse, but also want to verify it with facts, which is really annoying. In fact, this is just creating trouble for yourself. The best way is to "leave it to fate" and "let people do what they want." The so-called "if you're not foolish and deaf, you won't be a head of household." This is the attitude that we ordinary people should have. If you want to be smart, or pretend to be insightful, and insist on breaking through their back walls, then you can't remedy it, and you can't resist it. You are just asking for trouble.

Enough small talk, national affairs are important. Now that Peiping and Tianjin are so tight, and it is heard that once a certain branch president arrived, the hearts of the people in Peiping and Tianjin were greatly stabilized, and the Japanese offensive was suddenly eased, just like eating a dose of cooling medicine for a fever, making people feel refreshed all over. It really has unexpected effects.

News Brought by the Spring Breeze (Continued) 249

— Ping

Awakened from a daze by the sound of knocking, I opened my eyes to find the sunlight filling the window. A friend burst in, saying, "The dishes at Wanhua Tower will sell out soon, hurry up and let's go have morning tea."

Emerging from Wanhua Tower, we walked to Jinshan. It was nearly noon, the sun beat down, we took off our jackets, wiped our sweat, and strode forward. The new surroundings certainly made me forget the sorrow I left in Shanghai.

Jinshan Temple isn't as magnificent as Lingyin Temple in Hangzhou, probably gaining its name from the story of the White Snake flooding Jinshan. At the foot of the mountain is the Fahai Cave, said to be where Fahai attained enlightenment, likely also a tool for the monks to collect money. The entire Jinshan isn't as joyous as its name suggests. Climbing the Jinshan Pagoda, one can see the white-thread-like Yangtze River. The peak of Jinshan is right here. We sat atop the pagoda, our collars open to the wind, as my friend pointed out Jiaoshan and Ganlu Temple. Our plan was to visit them in the afternoon, but due to the unavailability of boats, we changed our itinerary to the Purple Bamboo Grove and Zhaoging Temple. As for Jiaoshan and Ganlu Temple, one glance from Jinshan Tower was probably the last we’ll see of them.

Proceeding from Jinshan Temple, we passed through a willow-lined path straight to the First Spring Under Heaven. The monks were warm and welcoming, the First Spring Under Heaven was cool, thick, and refreshing. The four of us chatted with the presiding monk in broken Zhenjiang dialect, losing track of time for two hours. It's a pity I can't grow old in this village, sipping tea every day, chatting idly with the old monk.

In the afternoon, we hired rickshaws to visit Purple Bamboo Mountain, a newly built automobile road in Zhenjiang. After leaving the city, the flat road seemed buried in the middle of ten thousand mountains. The rickshaw meandered forward, watching the endless road stretch on, sitting in the rickshaw felt like a vague dream.

The Purple Bamboo Grove is built in a mountain depression. Viewed from the plains, it appears only as towering ancient trees. Ascending the stone steps, the temple foundation gradually rises with the mountain's incline. At the highest point is the Yijiang Pavilion, with a view far surpassing Jinshan Temple, because nearby are countless nameless hills, quietly elegant,

Page 21

and far removed from the world, with the faint sound of bells wafting over, we sat in the Yijiang Pavilion, unwilling to leave.

"Ping, this place is great for treating lung ailments. You can borrow a small room from the abbot, and in two months, your wife won't recognize you," my friend said.

I didn't answer, staring ahead, though I didn't actually see anything. Before my eyes was just an impenetrable dark cloud.

Although C was usually joking and carefree, in such situations he was particularly perceptive. Seeing that an awkward atmosphere was about to develop, he grabbed my hand and said, "Let's quickly visit Zhaoging Temple and order some songs at the Pagoda Forest." He even mimicked the pidgin Zhenjiang dialect, and with forced laughter, we continued forward on the avenue.

But my friend's words still resonated in my ears, in rhythm with the cartwheels. People spend exorbitant sums of money to feign illness, some even travel abroad for ailments that Chinese medicine can't cure. On the cart, I recalled my brother's words: "The poor can't afford to be sick, being sick isn't for the poor!"

I am working while ill, my brother is studying while ill. The sorrow I left in Shanghai returned to my memory. As for Zhaoging Temple, I merely climbed up and down the stone steps.

Mr. Jiamenglú, "Four Quatrains on an Rubbing of a Buddhist Association's Bronze Bell Presented to the Japanese Earthquake Memorial Hall." Grief and indignation overflowed in his words. Disregarding my own inadequacy, I respectfully follow his rhymes. My intent is slightly different, hoping that the sound of the bell across the sea, like a lion's roar, can awaken our deeply slumbering compatriots! The bandits from Jiangnan just ceased their eastward advance, and now the northern gate's lock is opened again: The generations-old feud between Wu and Yue is forged into iron! Hearing the bell's sound, courage collapses.

Bearing the burden of the people and the nation's pain, Half of the land is entrusted to heaven's calamity. A different meaning can be found in rise and fall, The White Horse Temple is rebuilt as a Buddhist field.

A Small Piece of Land's Dispute 251

— Bai Fu

Although the island nation's Royal Army has not yet reached Beiping, our Beiping intellectuals and patriots have long transported batches of valuable books, instruments, and specimens to the South. Some schools have even moved entirely to the safer South to study. Relying on heaven and Bodhisattvas, they have safely retreated. I believe that if Beiping could be moved, they would move the entire city to the South.

While these many patriots safely retreated, only the Beiping Library remained unmoved. It is certainly a strong institution. But according to the director, the reasons for not moving are: first, because there are too many books to move; second, because many intellectuals in Beiping rely on the library to make a living. By copying books and writing articles in the library, they can earn a living by submitting them to newspapers and publishing houses. Moving the library would take away these intellectuals' livelihood, causing them to face unemployment. Third, our director believes that even if the island nation's Royal Army reaches Beiping, it is only a political issue, unrelated to culture. The Royal Army won't necessarily destroy his cultural institution—the library that intellectuals rely on for a living. Yes, the fall of a nation is indeed due to political issues. Perhaps when the Royal Army arrives in Beiping, they will not only refrain from destroying his cultural institution but also issue a commendation to our director for diligently preserving culture by not moving the books.

However, the Beiping Library is certainly stronger than those patriots who fled in terror at the sight of the Royal Army. Let's set that aside for now and just talk about those patriots who prepared to retreat safely. According to reports, since the Ministry of Education organized the Labor University Management Committee, there has been no solution for its disposition. National universities in Beiping, fearing the danger to Pingjin, have sent representatives to the capital to request the Ministry of Education to allocate the Labor University site for use in relocating their schools to the South. A national university in the South, seeking to develop its future, has also sent representatives to the Ministry of Education for consultations. The various parties have been arguing for many days… etc. Goodness gracious, this small piece of land has caused our patriotic intellectuals to argue for many days. Although no swords or guns were drawn, the back-and-forth of verbal battles may have led to parched lips and exhausted tongues. But after this long and inconclusive battle of words, the patriots of Beiping, those educators! have failed. Therefore, they returned to Beiping disappointed. It is said that due to the tense situation and the danger to Pingjin, they will advance the start of summer vacation!

That small piece of land finally belongs to So-and-so University and the Northwest Agricultural and Forestry College. Apart from the unhappiness of the Beiping patriots, this writer also feels dissatisfied that the Northwest Agricultural and Forestry College has been allocated this small piece of land. It is said that the Northwest Agricultural and Forestry College's educators, also patriots, were concerned about the fall of the East and West and wanted to develop the Northwest early to strengthen national defense. As the name suggests, the Northwest Agricultural and Forestry College, committed to developing the Northwest, should go to the Northwest. However, they insist on competing for land in Shanghai, which is full of foreigners. Shanghai, in addition to being developed by our noble compatriots over thousands of years since opening up to foreign trade, has also undergone painstaking development by foreigners. Now, roads extend in all directions, tall buildings stand in rows, and it has become one of the world's major commercial ports. Does it still need the patriots of the Northwest Agricultural and Forestry College to develop it? Perhaps Shanghai is a place where all types of people gather, a place where Eastern and Western cultures converge. Since its commerce has reached the level of a major international port, its universities and schools, large and small, are the best in the country. This is the center of modern Chinese culture. The Northwest Agricultural and Forestry College is also one of our new and emerging cultural enterprises in China, so naturally, it must be established in the cultural center to promote the glory of Chinese national culture, right?

Slowdown 252

— Jin Xin

The God of Love, Venus, has been very annoyed recently. She thought, "I am a goddess! How can I work tirelessly like a machine every day?" Her job, of course, is to connect the "golden threads of love" between men and women. But recently, because free love has become so popular in the human world, her work is not as leisurely as it used to be. She wants to lighten her workload, so she pleads with men in the world:

"Men of the world, I beg you! Don't love those demon-like women anymore! They will drain your blood, suck your strength, and consume your great spirit."

She also says to the women of the world:

"Gentle and beautiful women of the whole Earth! I urge you not to love those rogue-like men anymore, okay? They will ruin your beauty, bind your will, and deprive you of your freedom. They are like bird catchers. As soon as you fall in love with one of them, you will be caught in his trap, and you will become his property entirely."

However, the men and women of the world, as if not hearing her advice, are still happily loving each other, pursuing the taste of love. Not only have love affairs not decreased at all, but they are increasing day by day. The God of Love is greatly disappointed; the leisure she hoped for will not materialize. She is both angry and tired. In the end, she decides to go on a passive slowdown.

From then on, although the God of Love, Venus, is still performing her duties, she is not as serious as she used to be. She often connects the threads of love incorrectly or breaks them halfway, causing the young men and women of the world to feel countless sorrows and worries.

Shop Clerk's Communication

Loss of Property 253

Dear Editor:

I am a newly trained shop assistant in a cigarette shop, only a month out of my apprenticeship. Last week, I encountered an extremely unfortunate incident that I cannot justify. One morning, the shop owner ordered me to exchange one hundred yuan of small silver coins (double dimes). This is a very common occurrence recently. I counted the banknotes, stuffed them into my short-sleeved shirt pocket, and went out. After passing through the Maijiaquan area, I turned towards the Daigou Bridge. When I arrived at my destination, I reached into my pocket for the money. It would have been better if I hadn't touched it. The result of this touch made me cry involuntarily. It turned out that the pocket on my short-sleeved shirt was two-thirds broken. Only two corners of the pocket were still connected to the shirt itself. The bottom part was completely detached. At the time, I didn't know the details, so I put the money inside and walked on the road, causing it to be lost. Seeing that the exchange of small silver coins was impossible, I had to return to the shop crying and explain the situation to the owner. Who knew that the boss, upon hearing this news, showed no sign of forgiving me? He severely scolded me and even asked the guarantor to write a letter to my father, trying to negotiate compensation. My father is a low-ranking clerk in the Hankou Military Medical Office, with a monthly income of only over ten yuan, which is not enough to cover monthly expenses. Where would he get the money to pay this compensation? I really don't know how to solve this matter! So these days, I've been restless and unable to eat or sleep. Sir, what is the proper way to resolve this matter? Please give me a response in a short time. Sincerely,

Zhuang Zipei

×　　×　　×

Editor's note: In theory, Zhuang should be held responsible for

Page 22

compensation for this matter. Because the shop owner hired a clerk, he naturally has the right to ask him to handle business. If a clerk could lose property under his care during his duties and not be held liable for compensation, then the social order would not be able to be maintained. However, according to the letter, Zhuang's shop owner's attitude is good. His "lack of forgiveness" and "severe scolding" are unavoidable for most people. He asked the guarantor to write a letter to your father to "negotiate compensation," which, although aimed at compensation, still leaves room for negotiation in the amount because of the words "negotiate." The words "find a way" suggest that there may be flexibility in the timing and method of payment. We believe that you should also ask your father to come forward and negotiate on the basis of these four words, "negotiate" and "find a way." Request a discount on the amount and ask for a feasible payment schedule. This would already be considered generous by the shop owner. Hoping to avoid compensation altogether is impossible. The future is long, and your future is worth more than just one hundred yuan!

Here, we want to warn all shop clerks to be careful and cautious with the property they handle during their duties. Because once a loss occurs, even if it is known that you did not embezzle it, you cannot escape the responsibility of compensation, whether legally or emotionally.

Finally, we must also say to the public, "You should not keep lost property for yourselves." You should know that for you, it is unexpected wealth that you can live without. But for the loser, it may often lead to despair. Appropriating lost property is legally less severe than theft. However, morally, it is more severe than theft. Because the victims of theft are mostly members of the propertied class, while losers often include poor young men like Zhuang. The responsibility for theft can be avoided with the words "force majeure," but the responsibility for loss is undeniable.

Fiction

The Life of the Five Beauties (13) (Continued) 254

— Ling He

Twelve. A fragment of life three

One spring afternoon, the warmth of the sun poured in softly, most easily leaving one with a lazy languor. The concubine Liu, probably because of the excessive heat, finally woke up again. She listlessly moved her body slightly, and felt her entire body to be clammy, covered in sweat. She stretched out her hand and pressed the electric bell a few times, as a gust of cold air rushed into the bedding, followed by a violent fit of coughing, and when the maid He Xiang came in, she noticed fresh streaks of blood in her phlegm.

He Xiang walked to the side of her bed, her eyes filled with passion, tears hanging in the corners of her eyes, as her lips were slightly parted, panting on the pillow. He Xiang really had a good heart, and had been secretly worried for her since the concubine Liu had started coughing up blood a month ago, even more than once. However, she didn't try to dissuade her much now, as she had said a few earnest words a few times before, but the concubine Liu always smiled, clearly not taking her words to heart, and had even replied with a bitter smile once:

"Stop nagging, I know you mean well, but even if I listened to your words, would you be able to live a poor life with me? Silly girl!"

These kinds of words, though not scolding her, always left her feeling a little unappreciated. So now, she simply sighed and went into the bathroom to prepare a bath for the concubine Liu.

The concubine Liu sat in the tub, examining her body, which had indeed become much thinner recently. So she immediately recalled the mad attitude of manager Gu last night, and everything went black before her eyes, but she immediately tried to stop this thought, and began pouring warm water onto her bosom.

He Xiang knocked twice on the door, before lifting the curtain and standing in the room. She said softly:

"Young Master Zhang came once at nine o'clock today, it was really ridiculous, coming so early. Then he came again at eleven o'clock, trying to barge in, saying he had to see you, Miss..."

"Which Young Master Zhang are you talking about?"

"The one who sent a picture once."

"Sent a picture? There are so many pictures, how can I know who you mean?"

"Then should I get it for you to see?" She said, starting to run outside, but the concubine Liu shouted to stop her:

"Who wants to see it? I am asking when Master Gu left?"

"Probably around eleven o'clock. He told me not to disturb you. He was walking to the door when Young Master Zhang came in."

As the concubine Liu sat in front of the vanity table, facing the mirror, she put on the string of pearls manager Gu had recently given her. Frankly, the amount that she was violated last night was indeed more than that string of pearls was worth.

Suddenly, the phone rang, followed by the happy laughter of the maids. Then He Xiang came in and said:

"Miss! That Zhang person called again, saying he will be coming to visit you soon." Then she added quickly: "Men like that are rare. But he really is very handsome. They all say he is both young and good-looking." Soon, she smiled mischievously and went out.
