Film Supplement

The Private Life of Mae West 255

— Wen Ying

Paramount's Sex-Symbol Star

Romantic Lead in "She Done Him Wrong"

"She Done Him Wrong," recently screened at the Guanglu and Lanxin theaters, caused a sensation in the United States and led to the "Go West" slogan. Of course, the general public has already been captivated by its star, Mae West. Mae West's style has created a unique niche in the American film industry, enough to alarm moralists and overturn playboys. She completely transcends the abstract realm of sex appeal and specializes in the tangible allure of sex to attract men. And according to the conviction derived from general observation, the target Mae West wants to move is not the soft-skinned, tender young man, but hard-boiled men over middle age who have experienced the vicissitudes of life. She herself is in middle age and her style is extremely hard-boiled. The Lady Lou she plays in "She Done Him Wrong" has large breasts and even fuller hips, which are not what young men truly seek; what they want is just a beautiful face and a slender figure!

What is said here is, of course, not what moralists are willing to discuss, because Mae West and moralists are fundamentally irreconcilable. Mae West has had many encounters with moralists in the United States, but Mae remains true to herself, unwavering and not showing the slightest sign of surrender. Mae West's slogan is "Give him as much sex as possible, and not simple, ordinary sex, but Mae West style sex." So on the stage or on the screen, she puts sex appeal first. Because of performing sex appeal, she was not tolerated by the moralists or church people in small cities, so she was imprisoned for ten days on Blackwell's Island. Many of the political dance dramas she starred in were banned or detained. She had ample opportunities to escape punishment, but she bowed her head obediently and walked through the prison door. Her reason was that imprisonment enhanced her fame. Sure enough, her deeds were widely reported by newspapers across the United States, and her desire for fame was finally fulfilled.

But it is said that Mae West's own nature is not so lewd and romantic. Just as people see her plump body on the screen, weighing a full one hundred and sixty pounds, but in reality, she weighs only one hundred and eighteen pounds, and the rest is dressed up by Paramount costumes. When she leaves the theater and the crowd and returns to her secret private residence, she returns to her original appearance. She is just an ordinary woman! There is nothing too hard-boiled about her. She can also be coquettish or cry, and she is also very emotional, not too eccentric. Her only hobby is diamonds. Her fingers, neck, and chest are often covered with dazzling things, more than the brass studs on the dog collar!

Mae is married. Her husband's name is James Timony, a famous lawyer in New York, full of wit and talent. Timony and Mae West were both born and raised in New York, both from humble backgrounds. Mae first met Timony when she asked Timony to resolve a small case. After they met, they were like magnets and iron filings, firmly attached and inseparable.

In addition to acting, Mae can also write. She often revises or completely changes the screenwriter's script because the script is not sexually suggestive enough to suit her identity. Timony also helps a lot in this regard. And Mae West's success is largely due to Timony's vigorous support.

Film Review

Review of "Awakening" 256

— Yan Nan

If the audience is not forgetful, they will surely feel that this film "Awakening" is derived from Jane Eagels' "Father's Sin." The reason why the Central Film Censorship Committee praised it is because every aspect of this film surpasses the records of any small company production. On this point, I do feel that the general trend of the Chinese film industry is moving towards the bright road.

The story is about a village girl who meets a primary school teacher. Later, because of her parents' forced marriage, she disregards everything and runs away with him to Shanghai to live together. Tempted by material things, the young man becomes enamored with a dance star. At the same time, he loses his job, and he goes to Beiping with the dance star. The village girl has given birth to a son but cannot afford to raise him, so she has to become a dance hostess. The young man is abandoned by the dance star in Beiping, and she takes away all his property. Helpless, he can only beg his way back to Shanghai. By then, his wife has been divorced, and only a six-year-old orphan remains at home. Only then does he greatly awaken. He exchanges labor for food and clothing, and he becomes an extremely honest person. His son also receives help and goes abroad to study. The fallen village girl, due to a conflict between dance patrons, is unjustly accused. Because one of her old customers is a major thief, she is sentenced to fifteen years in prison. She is released from prison when her son returns home to marry, during the time the whole family is watching. The young man never forgets the love of the village girl. He learns that she has become a beggar and immediately goes to the snowy ground to bring her back.

Ideologically, this film can indeed serve as a wake-up call for young people, tearing down the modern mask, revealing the intoxication of infatuation, and at the same time promoting ethics and morality. This type of work is rare.

Director Wen Yimin can be said to have improved ten thousand times compared to before. However, it is a very good film, but it does not take a new path. Using a dance hall to describe the city inevitably falls into clichés. Technically, the director has learned the strengths of European and American films, and it is not forced at all. The cinematography is also very good, able to harmonize yin and yang, strength and gentleness. The set is also quite impressive. The flying paper and dancing cloth in the room are because there is no glass greenhouse, which seems excusable, but it can also be said to be negligence. Although the camera lens is good, there is one major flaw in the whole film, which is that the actors move too fast, walking like running. There are not many subtitles, but there are also many aphorisms.

Fan Xuepeng's performance is the best. Her portrayal of the pain suffered by a village girl, her efforts to try to be modern, is very moving. In particular, her repentance after "awakening" is quite subtle. The supporting roles are relatively inferior in comparison, but they are actually all very good.

This film does not fail as a good work because it is able to have the power of satire.

Strictly speaking, there are still some small loopholes in ideology and technique. To protect domestic films, especially those produced by small companies, I will not mention them. Generally speaking, those who are interested in domestic films will all find it good.

Review of "Woman and Jewels" JewelRobbery 257

— Ling He

Indeed, William Powell's appeal in movies is not insignificant. Yesterday, the audience at the Cathay Theater was noticeably larger than usual. Because of this, we might as well start by examining the actor's performance.

Of course, we must admit that Powell's acting skills are indeed outstanding, and he plays the leading role in the film. Taking "Woman and Jewels" as an example, his performance is truly pleasing. When he leads a group of robbers to loot a jewelry store, he is so alert and agile, and at the same time, elegant and dashing, as if trying to portray the special demeanor of a so-called master thief. We have seen many such master thieves on the screen, but are they exactly as he portrays them? Unfortunately, we do not have that kind of experience, so we cannot rashly judge. However, in Romantic works of art, people are often amazed. Therefore, Powell here gives the audience a relatively deep impression. Later, he courts the woman, showing off a lot of jewelry in front of the Baroness, leading to a tender engagement. Regarding these, we also acknowledge his thorough "craftsmanship." However, those who do not understand the fickle love games of "golden quality" will not be moved by him.

I remember a few years ago in the silent film "Prosperity Dream," he played a very loyal and honest small businessman at a gas station wearing glasses. That kind of loyal and sincere performance is still unforgettable to me. But here, he transforms into an elegant and dashing master thief, but compared to the aforementioned film, it always feels insufficient.

Regarding the supporting roles, I don't think it is necessary to mention them one by one. A good film cannot succeed without good supporting roles.

However, the director's skills are also worth noting. The best scene is the robbery in the jewelry store. He portrays each of the robbers as shrewd and capable, while also not letting go of anyone being robbed. Of course, these scenes are entirely theatrical, without credible reality. However, he is able to pay close attention to the most minute details, which is not easy. Secondly, when the robbers appear at the Baroness's house, he intentionally sets up many doubts to raise the audience's tense mood. Also, disguising a suspect to look similar to the master thief is where the director shows off his cleverness. His ridicule of the Baron and the exposure of luxury also shows that he has quite a bit of artistic cultivation.

As for the story itself, it is clearly entirely fictional, but in its literary position, it has the special characteristic of "satire." However, it is only a well-intentioned "mockery" of real society, which the screenwriter certainly considers necessary. However, "women," "jewels," and "robbery" will naturally not be improved as a result. That's all.

Reader's Opinion

My View on "Rouge Market" 258

— Yi Bing

Incomplete Awareness, Unstrained Structure

Indeed, recent domestic films have shifted from martial arts and erotic themes to rural and urban aspects. But recently, it is obvious that the issue of women's liberation has become the subject of films, as can be seen in the advertisements of various companies. And "Rouge Market," filmed by the Star Film Company, is one of the best.

Regarding the awareness of the whole film, there are thorough aspects and vague aspects. Li Cuifen is an ordinary woman, so when Li Mingyi dies, her old mother is seriously ill, and there is no rice to cook at home, she resolutely throws herself into the role of a female employee. What is this for? It is only to make a living, and there is no slightest thought of "understanding society." Afterwards, Cuifen is deeply stimulated, so she fights against the evil environment and eventually opens a small shop for the enjoyment of the rich. Regardless of whether it is actually allowed, if women's employment is only this little bit, it is inevitable that there will be a lack of limited understanding.

The structure is also not tense; especially the last scene where Guohua and Cuifen meet again is boring. I suppose the screenwriter still has a trace of the traditional concept of "reunion" in his heart? Also, Cuifen was originally a very self-respecting woman, who resigned voluntarily because she did not want to be bullied and teased by others, which is quite fitting for her identity. But later, because Miss Yang persuaded her to understand society, she went to beg the company again, hoping to be hired. Although she did not succeed, is the only place to understand society a department store? Furthermore, the various types of women's occupations, such as switchboard operators and copyists, are shown one by one, which shows the director's ingenuity; but the insertion points are not as good as expected. I think the ending of the whole play would be best if Cuifen said "We are still friends" and then the black curtain gradually fell. Then, what kind of scene will unfold in the minds of the viewers? It is a pity that the screenwriter also neglected this.

Anecdotes from Charlie Chaplin's Childhood 259

— Zui Ying

Chaplin was very naughty as a child. He didn't care about his homework in class. The teacher shouted himself hoarse on the podium, teaching in many ways, but he was still appreciating the photos of movie stars in his hand. But his pair of flexible eyes constantly looked at the teacher's movements, and when he saw him walking over, he quickly flipped the photo over, like a blank piece of paper, pretending to be recording there. But his kind of hypocritical trick was eventually seen through by the teacher, but he was calm and unhurried, and even said to the teacher with a grin: "Teacher, this is a photo of a certain movie star, very precious, if you love her, I will give it to you."

Movie Novel The White Sister 260

— Si Ping

A Goldwyn production starring Helen Hayes

Sacrificing Honor and Happiness for Love

"I do not know," Angela lifted her head, meeting passionate, adoring eyes. Her alluring gaze swiftly lowered again.

"I know. He fell madly in love. What is the woman like?"

"What woman?" Angela, with guileless eyes, looked up at him.

"The woman he's in love with." He returned her glance ardently.

"I have not seen her," she murmured, scrutinizing her tea.

"I have seen her." He regarded her steadily. "She is very beautiful丨she has alluring eyes丨her nose is straight丨"

"You must be drunk," Angela said sincerely, but instantly regretted her blunder. "I often say the wrong thing. I often trouble Ernastus."

"Who is Ernastus?" he asked anxiously. The mention of the name seemed to dispel the spell that had enveloped them. They reached out their hands to part. Angela shyly withdrew her hand from his grasp.

"I am engaged to him," she said.

"Oh!" Giovanni exclaimed, as if relieved of a burden. "I thought丨perhaps you loved someone else!"

"Ah丨of course, I love him," Angela said simply. She glanced at the watch on his arm. "Heavens!" she cried, rising and enveloping herself in her shawl. "Where is Mina? I must go."

Giovanni helped Angela into a streetcar.

Mina, agitated, ran frantically back to the palace. She wished Angela had returned safely. But she was not at the palace! Her alarm was great, and she immediately put on a calm face, pacing back and forth in the garden waiting. Prince Schermond wandered to her side and asked if Angela was inside. She answered vaguely, and as she saw the Prince wander off, she heaved a sigh of relief.

Outside the high walls surrounding the garden, far from the large iron gates, she glimpsed a streetcar arriving and stopping. Angela's face looked out anxiously from the car window. Then, the car doors opened, and she slipped out of the car丨Giovanni followed. She paused and extended her hand.

Home
